"Even if there are wronged people, there is no way to resolve their grievances, so how can people feel secure about their future?

I have invited you here today because my heart, which is anxious, frustrated, and filled with indignation, cannot bear it and has to live with it.

Are we slaves? Or are we equal owners of this society?

The periphery of power is growing obese, while the case of those who are not is getting thinner, so I have no way of knowing the sentiment of today.

What is more suspicious is that I am even more frustrated that people's common sense is of no help to others and no help to themselves.

What does this indicate? Is it telling us to wait for the results? Is it telling us to guess and know?

Is the scene where silence flows because it wants a new history of reflection? Is it simply to see the destruction of the national spirit?

I want to ask if it is really necessary for us to have an era where one must not trust others to live.

The world is now, all countries regard justice as the foundation, and politics is based on it, and the promise is like life, and by that ordinance, people trust others, rely on themselves, and all people find comfort.

But we now do not have the same foundation as other countries.

It is only because I was wrong and you were wrong that this result is happening.

We have trusted people too much and feared power too much, so this phenomenon is happening even more prominently.

When you want to be treated as a master, you must act like a master. When a master cannot act like a master, the social order is destroyed, common sense disappears, and one's own authority faces challenges.

When one realizes oneself and becomes enraged, one already sees one's lonely self and feels that one has come to live in an unhappy world.

I did not care about my own position today. I just came out to you because I could not give up my life and hope.

The truth cannot be changed. If you follow the truth, you cannot be unhappy.

If you know you are the master, you must fight for the master's authority, and to seek trust, you must realize a new era of politics.

I have abandoned fear for that era. A worker who does his job well is our treasure, but a worker who will ruin the country is our enemy.

I insist that we must discard the dark heart of becoming a slave ourselves in the face of small threats or ridiculous compromises, even if we think of the past.

The tyranny of power is not truth. It is only the action of one who lacks conscience.

I will not think about why I am living in an unhappy world. I will go to the side where there is the truth that I will become happy. At that time, I will take all of you with me.

Until then, I ask you to endure even if there are many inconveniences, to have courage, and to face today's reality with wise judgment."

The emcee then introduced the next speaker.

"I will now introduce the standard-bearer of the anti-dictatorship struggle, the standard-bearer of democracy, the leader of the Daejung Party, Mr. Wolpa Seo Min-ho."

When the emcee's words ended, the hall became solemn.

The teacher's dignified appearance stood before the microphone and began to open his mouth. The audience responded with thunderous applause.

As the teacher's brilliant speech gained momentum, the microphone cord was cut by someone's trick.

The teacher, despite being seventy years old, captured the atmosphere of the hall with his own voice. The rally ended only after one o'clock in the afternoon.

The crowd dispersed, and when we were left alone, the speakers from Seoul and the candidates for the local party chapter chairman in Busan, a group of about ten people, came out to the bustling streets of Nampo-dong and ate seolleongtang (ox bone soup) for lunch, which the teacher who was the party leader had bought, and they relieved their fatigue with stories.

Everyone praised the rally for going well. The party leader, Mr. Wolpa, asked his secretary about the train time and then suggested that our group have a cup of tea at the largest coffee shop in Busan. Our group went into the Hyangchon coffee shop in Nampo-dong, which was on the side of a nearby street, and ordered coffee.

The customers in the coffee shop, realizing that the old gentleman in our group was the very famous Assemblyman Seo Min-ho, all shifted their gazes to our group. The group held onto the teacher and had a conversation until the time for his departure by train.

We also went to Busan Station to see him off. As the train departed, I became alone.

Returning to Yeongdo, as I entered the room, I immediately collapsed onto the bed and fell asleep. My sister, perhaps thinking my actions during the day were admirable, told the children not to make noise, covered my body with a blanket, and went out.

In the midst of a busy life, the daylight hours of winter passed quickly.

In my chest, I piled up an affection I had never felt for anyone before, under the name of my country, and nurtured that affection.

Another year passes, raising my age.

Whenever the strong sea breeze blew, spring was coming.

I realized that this year was the year of the presidential and parliamentary elections, and in my heart, which was now a political aspirant, joy and worry began to arise. I shouted at myself, who was like this.

"I do not fear others. I only fear myself."

In the late winter of the new year, close to spring, a message came from the central party. It was a notice of the Daejung Party's national convention.

I, as a delegate, took a train to Seoul with two friends who were also party members.

At the convention held at the annex of the Citizens' Hall, which was the convention venue, Assemblyman Seo Min-ho, the party leader, was nominated as the presidential candidate. The teacher accepted the absolute nomination of the party members and gave an acceptance speech. However, the era when an individual's courage or ability was not in the spotlight was an unfortunate era for a single talented person.

Not long after the national convention was over, the teacher, who was the party leader, had to think about whether to give up his candidacy due to the era's desire for a change of government.

People's expectations had to bring a moment of pain to one person for the sake of reality. Because of the legal situation at the time, the teacher had to leave the party leadership and the party.

At that moment, what he could comfort himself with was only the hope of his compatriots. He worried about the many people who had followed him at the last moment.

The news in the newspapers covered the teacher's whereabouts with interest, and his opponents laughed at him.

The teacher's ideology was that all people must fight against hypocrisy, and for that ultimate reason, he handed over the Daejung Party, which he had protected with his own strength, to the people who had been his closest comrades and aides until then.

It was the last moment to part while sharing a sad affection. He had the party seal, which had been stained with his hand for a long time, brought and stamped it on two National Assembly candidate nomination certificates, and then left the office.

On the two nomination certificates were Mr. Kim Dong-hyun of Cheongsong and Yeongdeok in the Gyeongbuk region, and Lee Sam-han of the Yeongdo district of Busan.

The Daejung Party, ahead of the election, elected Secretary-General Lee Mong as the new acting representative at an emergency political meeting and was issuing nominations for the National Assembly, which was coming up in about 20 days.

The April 27 presidential election began to heat up with the spring weather. Which side will win?

The confrontation between power and public sentiment—no city dweller could be optimistic. Since there had never been a peaceful change of government in the nation's tradition, among the city dwellers, some would decide the outcome of the election even during the election, saying that it was ruined because of the country bumpkins, while the naive citizens yearned for a change of government in their hearts.

May came. The presidential election, which had been very intense, came to an end, and the deadline for registering as a candidate for the National Assembly election was announced in the newspapers. I, who had held the nomination certificate in my hand before anyone else, had to worry.

The cost of the posters alone was over 100,000 won, but I didn't even have 100,000 won in my possession. In my naive heart, no matter how much I thought about it, I couldn't think of anyone who would chip in even 10,000 won and tell me to run.

And yet, I didn't want to show this shabby state to others shamelessly, and with a calm heart, I came to face that day in May.



16. The Reason I Could Not Fear Others

The morning of May 5th arrived.

In my chest, a pitiful feeling that I could not handle myself piled up. At this moment, I called two friends who were local party members and lived in the neighborhood and consulted with them. Only then did I hurry to register. A sense of mission arose in my chest that I had to go the way I was going, regardless of victory or defeat.

After making the decision, a natural, fateful temperament was arising in my heart. A voice that said never to be afraid struck my chest.

When did I ever live with money, and with whose help did I live? The goddess of fate finally opened the way for me to go, with only that kind of guts.

On the 6th, I barely managed to pay the poster fee before the deadline and finished registering. That evening, comrade Choi Hee-soo, who was the chairman of the Daejungdang Daedeok and Yeongi local party chapters and who had had contact with me in the party, came to visit unexpectedly.

I hired a Mr. Mo, a former high school social studies teacher, as my campaign manager, and with a few foremen from the labor market and my friend Yoo Mu-jong, who ran a barbershop, I prepared a staff and entered the election campaign.

On the 7th, a few people who had no experience in elections gave their opinions and made a campaign bulletin and submitted it to the regional election management committee.

Thinking about it, the work to be done in succession was like a mountain, but the fatigue piled up and I immediately got tired.

On the morning of the 8th at 9 o'clock, my whole body was as heavy as a thousand pounds, and sleepiness began to come to my eyes. In my lodging room, which was my campaign office, I stretched out my two legs and lay down, and immediately fell into a deep sleep.

Around 10:30, I woke up to a clamor. The campaign manager, the staff, and comrade Choi Hee-soo were flustered. It was because the joint policy speech was scheduled for this afternoon.

They, who had not seen me prepare a speech even once, were flustered, seeing me snoring peacefully without any plan for the impending event. I was sad that I could have slept a little more, but at everyone's serious expression, I also got up and started to move.

First, comrade Choi Hee-soo, with a dumbfounded expression, laughed absurdly and asked how I would give the joint speech. The various people who had come to help with the election campaign without any compensation, seeing me hesitating, protested that they would go home.

Even if the afternoon's problem was to be solved in the afternoon, this immediate commotion had to be settled. I rummaged through the booklet sent with the party's policy materials, pretended to read foreign books I couldn't read, and slowly observed the other side's expressions.

After 12 o'clock, after eating the lunch my older sister had prepared, sleepiness came to my eyelids again. I wanted to put everything aside and lie down, but conscious of the eyes of the people next to me, I forced myself to change my expression.

At that time, comrade Choi urged me to go out quickly, taking the lead. He said I had to go to the speech venue in advance and get my face known to the people. When he said that, the people next to me got up from their seats, and I also got up.

My heart is on the verge of dying, like a cow being led to a slaughterhouse. And yet, thankfully, everyone surrounded me and followed me to the Namjung School playground near the streetcar terminus.

As my eyes met with strangers, my mind gradually became clearer. The school playground, 30 minutes before the speech time, was crowded with people, and the other candidates had already come out.

At comrade Choi's words to act with dignity, the other people also gave advice to me, a young man.

First, to look dignified, I took a position with my group on one side of the wall where it would be easy for people to see.

For the first time, while watching the time approaching anxiously, I created a speech in my head about my political views. What immediately came to mind was only the hope that my speech order would be later.

In fact, since I had no organized manuscript for the speech, I was feeling quite afraid. Having jumped into the election campaign with only one conviction, without ever having been a campaign aide for anyone, no easy method came to mind.

But the voice of myself, telling me not to be afraid, forced me to endure, however difficult it was. Moment by moment, a struggle to endure the time continued.

At that time, an announcement came out from the speaker. An official from the election management committee was repeatedly announcing over the microphone.

"The speech will begin shortly, so candidates, please come to the observer's seat next to the podium, and if you are a candidate's representative, please come with the candidate's seal and draw lots for the speech order."

The comrades who had gathered around me began to get excited.

Comrade Choi took my seal and went to draw lots for the speech order, and when he returned, he said "number 1" with an apologetic face. The moment I heard those words, my heart felt a shock as if it were sinking.

But I had no time to be flustered and hesitate. Is this also the work of fate? My heart immediately wanted to hide somewhere. But the candidate could not run away from the playground, nor could he avoid giving a speech.

My name was immediately called through the speaker.

I became like a person who had no choice, put strength in my stomach, and went up to the podium.

Many in the audience were watching me, and seeing that scene, I resolved not to be disgraced here and gathered my wits. Then, with my eyes wide open, I looked at the audience and bowed my head.

When applause erupted from all sides, for some reason, my body was shaking at that moment. I gathered my wits, brought the microphone close to my face, and opened my mouth.

"I am Lee Sam-han, the candidate of the Daejung Party, number 4, who came here to give the 10th speech with the number 10 in the 10th general election."

and bowed my head. The people, as if to welcome my greeting, clapped. I thought of my next words and opened my mouth.

"The fact that one person has been given the cross three times in this regional election is not my magic, but the will of God. To repay you for waiting in the cold weather, I will first tell you why I decided to run for the National Assembly.

There are many things that frustrate me in my heart. There are politicians, but there is no politics around us.

If you just sit and listen, there are many patriots, but in reality, the state of the country is not good. The people really have nowhere to trust.

I felt that the place where there are the most people who have been cheated and are beating their chests in frustration in the world is the land where we live.

So I wondered why this world, as it goes on, is not getting better but getting worse, and I wanted to find out what on earth the members of the National Assembly we elected have been doing in the National Assembly that there are so many wronged and sad people, and also, to reflect on the situation around us that cannot be neglected, I came out before you to run in a rather difficult election.

I am not someone who came out to gain fame because I have a lot of money like other people, nor am I boasting because I have a good record, nor am I someone who came out to teach someone because I have a good education.

I couldn't just stand by and watch the state of the world and the worrisome future of the country, so I, a person like me, came out knowing that it wouldn't work in this kind of world, but my young conscience couldn't just ignore my country, so I came out saying I would save the country, I would save the dying politics, and I put up a large sum of money, 5 million won, as a deposit, even though if you look at it, for someone like me, it would be a donation.

Since this election is an important one for our country and for us as individuals in our future lives, my determination was also unusually great, unlike others.

In this important election, I would like to ask you, the sovereign people of this land, not to be deceived by personal connections, the temptation of material things, or threats and appeasement, and even if you have not registered as a candidate yourself, to participate as a candidate, and also to tell those around you that this election is an important one, and to work together to create an election atmosphere where you must find for yourselves a person who can work for the country, a person with courage, a person with conscience, a person who can bring justice to life, and to work together to save the future of the country, as a citizen with a conscience, I would like to ask you.

To the voters who have stayed until the last person to listen to my speech despite the chilly weather today,

Even if I don't hear your words, I think I can guess what is in your hearts. I, too, am giving a speech here now, but my true feelings are exactly the same as yours.

I promise to fight against the contradictory politics of today, which does not protect law and conscience.

I will fight against the incompetent and cowardly pseudo-politicians who turn a blind eye to justice. For that very reason, I came out here today. You who think that guy is a decent guy, please clap. The weather is cold today, so my heart is cold."

and as I finished my words, laughter and applause erupted from the crowd. I brought out my next words.

"Looking at the world these days, everything I see is just heartbreaking and frustrating. Emergency measures and what not, they even put handcuffs on other people's consciences, and they boast about spending extravagantly, borrowing from outside, let alone saving what they have, and they say they are doing politics well, and when I see them making a fuss about making such shameless people leaders, tears even come to my eyes.

A society where talented people are not protected by that society, such a thing is not even in history books. What can happen if a naive person worries about people who have abandoned their conscience?

There are people who have amassed hundreds of billions of won without ever doing business. They are goblin chaebols. I wonder if this phenomenon is the magic of a club or the magic of swindling. In fact, people who don't know envy their lives. And on top of that, there are all sorts of things in the world.

It is a clear principle that many wronged people will arise, but when I see them beating their chests because they have nowhere to appeal, the pain is ringing in the heart of the powerless person with a conscience.

I decided to run for office to show by my actions that all of us compatriots must fight against our cowardly selves to put an end to these sad stories.

Those of you who came here have few who are in a worse situation than me. Unless you show your actions for your country, is there any need to predict that our future will be buried in darkness?

Even if no one can take responsibility and they try to get out of it, in the near future, we will suffer damage that will be difficult for us to recover from on our own.

I cannot stand by and watch this happen. I have experienced enough hardship in this land, more than anyone else. At those times, I have lived until today with the happiness of the future.

Now that future is in danger. The ones who can save it are you and me. Will you do it? Shall I do it? Whoever does it, it is a task that must be undertaken with a firm resolve.

Even at this moment, there will be some among my fellow candidates who do not understand what I am saying. I will say a word for those people as well.

In particular, those who have been around the political and government circles will have reflected their opinions a lot in the meantime.

But looking at the state of the country these days, it's this shape and this form. I would like to ask those people, if they have any conscience at all, not to bother thinking of excuses for today's society and to make a courageous decision for a new era.

And to the others, I also insist that this place should not be turned into a place like a speech contest venue.

I warn you that this is not an era where you can be proud of blocking the path of a talented person who wants to save the country. I would like to suggest to those who feel they cannot risk their lives to solve the difficult problems of the present to resign from this position today, although I am sorry.

What is important for us to see today is that the country is important, hope is important, and the truth is important. I confidently pledge to do these things before you, the candidates and voters.

As a person who has always respected the parliamentary activities of our country's politicians, Mr. Kim Doo-han and Mr. Seo Min-ho, I promise to walk the same path as them."

At that time, the bell announcing the time rang.

I continued with my final words of request.

"Everyone, when you return to your villages today, please convey my words. I promise to not only bring honor to our hometown but also to brighten the future of our country. Thank you."

My speech was over. Even the applause section of the other candidates clapped. The last speaker in the order of speeches went up to the podium, which was past sunset.

On the podium of the playground where dusk was falling, the speech of the last person ended on time. I began a difficult march with a body and mind that had become a complete wreck.

Worries and regrettable problems grew more and more numerous. Because of my status as an independent, my activities were limited to going back and forth between my house and the campaign office. If I tried to abide by the tricky election law, I couldn't even visit people I knew.

It was a situation where a bird in a cage had no choice but to appeal to the people on the outside with its expression.

All sorts of people came to the campaign office. Most of them, in the end, frankly demanded to exchange their votes for money. My heart was sore and painful at the desperate scene.

The election method felt like a government-controlled election, and many voters did not seem to want to think about the reality of tomorrow. While thinking about how much more hardship this country has to go through, I endured the time, relying only on 1% hope rather than 99% impossibility.

The judiciary and the executive branch frequently posted papers with warnings that they would severely punish election offenders on the street.

It was also funny to see myself, who had participated in the election without any support in the world's most difficult election law and was asserting my own claims. Most of the candidates just did the P.R. for the wrong government and only received applause from the voters.

I protested to myself, "Is this an election?", but there was no answer. In this frustrating heart, the second joint policy speech was held at Bongrae Elementary School in Yeongju-dong.

The weather was clear and the climate had warmed up. The audience filled the small school playground. My speech order was fifth. After listening to the speeches of four people, my turn came. I went up to the podium.

Perhaps because I had been so nervous and talked so much, my throat was completely hoarse, and my anxiety reached its peak.

The audience clapped and urged me to give my speech. I slowly gathered my strength, cleared my throat, and opened my mouth.

"I gave the tenth speech at the speech rally held at Cheonghak Elementary School the day before yesterday. By the time my turn came, I had heard the speeches of nine people.

They all, like speakers at an elementary school speech contest, acted as spokesmen for the Yushin government, without any alternative, just telling people to endure, and they just said things that seemed to flatter the people in power today, and when I saw them just having the people they had brought with them by paying them to clap, I was so disgusted by their speeches that anger welled up in my heart.

At that time, when my turn came, I yelled at the innocent microphone a little, and so my voice is so hoarse that I'm sure it's uncomfortable for you to listen to me.

But I, too, came up here with an anxious heart, thinking about the society and the future of our country, so I ask for your understanding and cooperation for the time given.

My assertion is that we should first support and elect a person who can solve the difficult and hard things we are facing one by one, rather than just being deceived and electing someone who is good at making excuses and only suffering a dirty fate.

Let's not just repeat the tedious work of doing Yushin for generations of our children, and of being deceived and deceived again while understanding the Korean-style democracy in a state of insufficient hope, and of closing our mouths and enduring and enduring again even if it's unfair, but let's elect a smart and courageous person to try to have a world-class democracy and make a first-class country, that is my conviction.

We must ask that you do not commit the difficult act of electing a person who wants to be a master when the election is to elect a worker who is a member of the National Assembly of a country.

Among the people who came out in this election, it seems that there are people who are worthy of being 1st and 2nd among those who came out with the expectation that they only need to be 1st or 2nd thanks to the current election law.

Even while engraving in my heart the anxiety that I cannot speak the truth as it is at the scene where the law is presented because of the reason that even a bad law is a law, I put up 5 million won, which is a very large sum of money in my life, as a deposit, and came out saying that the country should not be like this, but there are only frustrating things to tell you about myself.

The only guaranteed way to conduct a public election campaign is to have four joint speech opportunities, but that is only 20 minutes long, so if you add up all four, it's only 80 minutes.

The venue is also not something I can choose at will, but at a designated place, and the order is decided by drawing lots for my luck, so I am at a loss.

If I pick badly, I have to appeal my patriotism, which is crying out in my heart, while looking at an empty playground where all the people have left, and even if I pick well, in front of the applause section that the rich people and the people who play around the power bring, I have to think of my own situation and cry, so what on earth should I do about this pitiful man's situation!

And some people spend a lot of money even though they know it's an election where you can't spend money. To put it simply, in a seven-person race, there are people who are completely free, people whose hands are tied, people whose feet are tied, and as for me, I am in a situation where I have to follow all the rules with both my hands and feet tied.

Is this some kind of obstacle course? If you can just judge fairly, please check. I am number one.

But it doesn't seem to be an obstacle course. So, out of human greed, aren't the other people violating it?

I don't know the reason, and when I ask the judge because I don't know the reason, do you know what he says? Those people's words are even more wonderful. It seems like a funny game. They say in the newspapers that they will definitely have a fair election this time, but is this method a fair election?

I am not talking like this now because I don't think I will be elected to the National Assembly. I am shouting out of anxiety when I think of the country, the position of my compatriots, and history."

As I confirmed the difficult scene of my face convulsing while trying to maintain my hoarse voice, I confessed the facts that had accumulated in my heart to those around me and tried to turn people's attention to the scene of the facts. Every time I added strength, applause kept bursting from the crowd.

When I finished my speech and came outside, a huge crowd surrounded my footsteps. I am doing my best for my own suffering and sacrifice, without understanding the intentions of the people who are not trying to distinguish reality correctly.

As the election day approached, the atmosphere among the people changed. Money was rampant, and even an atmosphere of fear was being created.

In the midst of that, I just feel that I have nothing to rely on. And yet, my comrades just encouraged the complaints of the campaign workers, saying that they had to use their funds. I became worried. And yet, difficult things just kept happening here and there.

A woman who was a campaign organizer came to my house in the evening and pleaded with me about her pitiful situation, with tears streaming down her face. She said her husband's workplace had declared that he should either control his wife properly or leave the job.

She cried, telling me about her angry husband's behavior, asking what would become of her. I comforted that woman.

My candidacy was difficult to realize conscience and justice, and it was creating a result of persecuting those with conscience and justice.

In Seoul, five comrades from my Daejung Party days came down to Busan to help me. And conscientious people, whom I had never met before, came from Seoul, Daegu, and Daejeon.

They all exaggerated in the same way, saying that public opinion and popularity for me were good, but my heart could not escape from gloom.

A new fear that I had never felt before began to arise. Is it a bankruptcy for my own comfort, or is it a self-defense to serve the country in the future, even if it disappoints the naive people? There were many difficulties in making a decision at a crossroads.

As this went on, the final election day was only three days away. Those three days were more painful to me than death. A certain degree of composure began to be restored in my heart.

I had no choice but to appease the core members who had been working so hard for the organization until now. So I called them all together at the same time.

I frankly confessed my current feelings.

"I don't want to deceive you. My position is a little different from the other candidates.

Most of the other candidates are people that the other side likes. I am the opposite now.

My own bankruptcy is something I have prepared for, but the clear fact that this will leave behind will not give me any excuse in the future.

My true heart wants to stand where you expect me to be. I know that the network and connections of the organization that you, who have no experience in campaign work, have created in a short period of time, thinking of me, are considerable.

I also know that even if I am not elected, the public's attention is on me.

But the problem is that there is no simple thing that will follow the action I have to choose at this final stage.

It is whether you will carry the painful cross without regret. This is a state that has not been decided for us."

The core members who had gathered in one place, unlike a moment ago, did not open their mouths. Silence flowed over their faces.

Other people also knew the election law, and because they knew that the candidate they were working for was a conscientious person whom the ruling power at the time most feared. I began to convey my intentions again.

"I want to understand you in any case.

From this moment on, I am resolved not to resent it even if I join hands with another candidate."

I revealed my true heart.

The people who had gathered with some expectation left the office listlessly with disappointed faces.

The time of suffering begins to flow very slowly.

The news that came in was the departure of the lower organizations. The word "best" was no longer left for our group.

On the day the voting began, I entrusted my work to the campaign manager who would remain in the office, and I went out to the intercity bus terminal to leave Busan with comrade Lee Dong-yeol, who had come down from Seoul and stayed by my side until the last day. My heart wanted to go far away somewhere.

Where should I go? Without even thinking about the direction, I got on the bus that was leaving right away and began to look at the destination of the bus. The bus, which had left the city, ran on the gravel road that stretched towards Yangsan. About two hours later, I got off near Yangsan Tongdosa Temple.

Even while walking along the road at the entrance of Tongdosa, where clear water flows, I felt sad in my empty heart. But I did not regret my past actions.

I needed alcohol to soothe my lonely heart. In front of comrade Lee and me, empty soju bottles piled up one by one. By the time we left the bar, it was difficult to support our bodies. A passing taxi took us to the nearby Tongdosa Hotel.

When the two people regained consciousness, it was the morning after being drunk. On the television screen in the room, the nationwide vote counting situation was still being broadcast. Fortunately, the vote counting for the Jung-gu and Yeongdo-gu districts of Busan, where I had run, was over.

My heavy heart began to feel refreshed. Even as I regained my senses, I couldn't think of what to do for my next action.

The two people who came out of the hotel ordered gukbap at a restaurant near the country market and filled their hungry stomachs with breakfast and lunch. I had to wash away the feelings that had accumulated in my sorrow with alcohol, going from one bar to another, as if I would do something.

I returned home only at night. My wife, who had been worried, looked happy to see me. The bustling house was quiet.

My wife, to comfort me, seemed to be doing her best, but as I entered the room, I immediately collapsed. My wife covered my body with a blanket.

The next day, I dressed myself neatly and went to the office to do the final clean-up after the election.

By noon, several people who had been core comrades came. Those people looked at me with apologetic expressions. I had to find words of comfort for such people.

I had a few bottles of alcohol bought and tried to cleanly forget the feelings that had built up. I handed over the envelopes with the small amount of money I had prepared to each person one by one.

"The election is over now. This envelope is my sincerity. Although it is a small envelope, I hope you will understand."

In the expressions of the people gathered in the seats, a bright and cheerful light began to emerge.

I poured alcohol into the glasses placed in front of each person one by one and for the first time told them my inner thoughts.

I continued, saying that there are still people with conscience living in this land, and that there are people who want to see the world rightly, and that people who are not even relatives have cast their votes without any expectation or reward for a bag of money or any material thing, and that I feel a sense of accomplishment in my actions.

I conveyed my heart that if I had spent money and bought votes to gain the attention of the world, I could have gotten a considerable number of votes for the cost, but that the result would have remained in my own conscience as a result of torturing me forever.

It was not a matter of my remaining pride, but my mission for the country that I had to find in the future. I really finished all the difficult work quickly.

As if he was getting drunk, one by one, they leave the office. Later, I was left alone in the empty office. Less than three days after the election was over, I had completely forgotten the things that had happened during the election period.

I began to plan my new work. From time to time, the people who had worked with me on the election came to me and praised me for cleaning up the difficult aftermath cleanly.

The month of December was very empty and lonely. Boredom and idle thoughts came flooding in, moment by moment.

Is it that I have luxury and vanity in my feelings? I felt the need to protect myself in order to dedicate a worthwhile action to my country until the moment my life remained.

A boundless dream began to arise anew in my chest.

I was tormented by futile delusions on the long winter nights that were unbearable, and when morning came, I always felt that I had not had enough sleep.

In the spring of 1980, I made a new start.

I started the business I had been doing until last year again. I also received a new business registration certificate.

At the newly reopened business, the people who had done business with me before began to come one by one.

I tried to forget all the things that had happened in my past actions through work and to return to the merchant I was a year ago.

Many of the people around me praised my determination and sincerity, and some people gave me courage, admiring my actions as if they were their own.

A month passes since the business reopened.



17. A Life Without a Spare

In my destiny, there could be no spare.

Even when I came to Busan, the immediate issue was the same as in Seoul. The only difference was that my poor sister, due to the bond of being siblings, reluctantly felt less of a burden for the time being.

But what I immediately learned was that it was no longer as easy to act in this town as it used to be. A certain fame followed me around.

When I walked down the street, people would glance at my face, and in alleys, middle or elementary school students would shout that so-and-so was passing by and not take their eyes off me until I was out of sight.

In a word, my situation was truly one of compounding misfortunes. But it was only me who had to overcome such things. I went around here and there, helping people I knew with their work and earning my daily wage.

I diligently created resumes and went around looking for any job, but I was rejected more often, being told that there was no position suitable for me because of my face.

I did not despair in any situation. Just as the proverb says that people without teeth chew with their gums, I abandoned the thought of relying on others and, confronting myself, found work day by day.

The only work that came to me was unpleasant, but I could not avoid such work either. I delivered things like soap, and in my spare time, I helped with other people's desired tasks and also started a scrap iron business.

In two months, after settling my food and lodging, I had some money left over. I once again thought about going up to Seoul to find my dream.

I resolved to do manual labor in Seoul just as I had in Busan. The thought that came to mind immediately was the saying, "If a person is born, send them to Seoul, and if a horse is born, send it to Jeju Island."

On a late autumn day, with several months' worth of lodging fees in my possession, I sat by the window of a regular express train with the word "express" on it, and as I felt the sentimental scenery passing by, I went up to Seoul with dreams and romance. A whistle came from my lips.

That day, I appeared on the streets of Seoul late in the afternoon. My appearance, in a newly tailored suit with a tie, looked dignified even to my own eyes.

When I even put on a pair of foreign-made sunglasses that I had gotten from a sailor I knew well one day, my appearance now was not the me of old, even in my own eyes.

When I stopped by the party headquarters, the comrades who saw me, who had appeared out of nowhere, were very surprised but also welcomed me.

That evening, I took the more than 10 comrades who were there to a cheap bar in nearby Gwancheol-dong. For the first time in a long time, I even ordered a side dish of fresh tofu and had the empty-stomached comrades fill their bellies with makgeolli.

Several pitchers were changed. Everyone, feeling a bit tipsy, the conversation grows long. The owner of the bar, because she knows the situation of our boisterous group well, shows an increasingly uncomfortable face, as if she is worried about the money.

I assured the bar owner not to worry about the cost of the makgeolli, which wasn't much, saying I would pay for the drinks today, and she stared at my cleaned-up appearance as if it were a marvel.

As the alcohol rose, my heart also swelled. When we came out of the bar, we all staggered and went our separate ways, waving our hands.

I, having become alone, had no need to hesitate on the street. Trusting the small amount of money I had, I had already made up my mind to spend one night at a nearby third-rate inn. My body, which had been tired all day, perhaps because of the alcohol, made the night pass quickly.

On that day, I found lodging for a while on the side of Sajik-dong, and I was thinking about the things I would have to face in my Seoul life. The next day, several young comrades from the party came to visit my lodging.

The cheap soju and dried squid leg snacks, over the flow of time, raise the heat in the empty stomachs.

Complaints about the world burst out. The conversation was about our surroundings regarding the party reorganization. People were trying to stir up trouble for some reason. For some reason, one by one, they start to get excited.

The people gathered here, for some reason, are plotting to shift this difficult problem onto me. I was the youngest among the people gathered at that time. And yet, even while they were getting excited themselves, they only watched my expression.

That afternoon, the party headquarters office was occupied by the mid-level central party officials, out of dissatisfaction with the independent personnel decisions made by the secretary-general at the last meeting.

The persuasion of the party's top committee member, who tried to handle this situation through compromise, also failed, and the party's elders left the party headquarters. The entrance door of the party headquarters was locked from the inside.

At that time, comrade Lee Kang-baek, who was the party's deputy secretary, suggested a hunger strike and proposed that no one go outside until their demands were met. The people who were there were even more excited by this opinion.

I, too, felt excited about the party's situation. And I also felt pity for the situation of the mentally weak party officials. It was the situation of the leadership, who could not prepare for the future, that created the problem. The excited people, as if they had gotten it from somewhere, drink alcohol.

The night deepened, and sadness piled up in my heart rather than satisfaction with reality. A rage arose that I had to say something.

I picked up the wooden handle of the mop used to wipe the floor. I opened my mouth, drunk.

"This situation is the fault of the current bureau chiefs, so the bureau chiefs of each department, if you resist, I will kill you, so come forward."

I shouted and demanded silence from those around me. At that time, there were some bureau chiefs who wanted to rebel at my harsh expression, but because of my supporters who were shouting and cheering, no one dared to challenge me personally.

I made the current bureau chiefs around me kneel on the spot. Perhaps because they felt an unavoidable danger, as they were people who only had an eye for situations in their Seoul life, a few bureau chiefs, while feeling the humiliation, watched my stern expression.

At yesterday's proposal that no one should eat until the demand was met, no one tried to leave the firmly closed door even after the night had passed.

Two intelligence detectives from the Jongno police station, having found out somehow, tried to call out the people they knew. When we warned them not to interfere in the party's internal affairs and refused the meeting, the police officers went back.

Mr. Lee Dong-hwa, who was a top committee member of the party, after 24 hours had passed since this incident, told us to return to our senses with a polite apology for the situation.

Mr. Lee Mong, who was the secretary-general and had exercised independent influence in the party's personnel reshuffle, recognized the reality and proposed that he would step down from his position as party secretary-general.

The hunger strike ended after confirming that. The resignation letters of all party officials were submitted.

The former secretary-general, Mr. Lee Mong, called me to a coffee shop individually and, with a very sad expression, opened his mouth.

He said that I was the most suitable person for the position of youth bureau chief, but because my current address was in Busan and I was in Busan at the time, he had appointed someone from Seoul, and then he came out coolly, saying that we should forget about such problems like men in the future.

I finally felt that this person was also a great vessel and, rather than the matter of one day, we agreed to work for the party in the future. The two people quickly washed away their awkward feelings.

I, who had parted with the former secretary-general, soothed my stomach with a bowl of bean-curd dreg bibimbap after two days and worried about the things to come.

As a result of the Daejung Party's political committee meeting being urgently convened the next day, the resignations of the bureau chiefs were accepted, and comrade Lee Won-soo, the chairman of the Gyeongbuk and Uiseong local party chapters, was appointed as the acting secretary-general.

With the new party reshuffle, the party's affairs began. I would leave my lodging in Sajik-dong and, while visiting the office of the Daehan Hongikhoe in Naeja-dong, Mr. Kim Woo-je's house, and the party headquarters, two months passed, and the money in my possession was running out again.

I was determined to start some kind of money-making work every day, but I couldn't actually put it into action. When I met with my comrades and the conversation started, I would forget about the urgent problem of living.

It was one day when I was wandering in a fruitless dream. In the end, I began to pack my bags. A few days before the Lunar New Year, with no money in my possession, I barely managed to take the train to Busan.

My comrades, who did not know my situation, held onto me, saying that the party's innovation would not happen without me, but no one's words moved my heart. I really did not want to leave Seoul.

I loved my country, I loved my affiliated party, and I loved my comrades. If it were a situation where I could stay because of an excuse, I wanted to find any excuse. But my situation separated me from my dear comrades.

On the day I left Seoul, about 10 of my party comrades and friends outside the party whom I had made friends with came to Seoul Station to see me off.

Because of the circumstances that we couldn't speak of, we tried to find comfort in soju glasses without any side dishes at a cheap bar near the station.

Comrade Choi Hee-soo, struggling in his own circumstances, got a train ticket and held it tightly in my hand, and on the day of departure, he comforted me with a sad expression, saying, "Let's work together after the New Year's holiday."

Comrade Lee Kyung-sik, who was the secretary to the president of the New Democratic Party, bought me two weekly magazines and handed them to me, telling me to read them on the train. Seoul Station was bustling with people leaving and coming into Seoul.

The comrades who came to see me off followed me to the ticket gate and comforted my troubled heart with a firm handshake. I pushed through the crowd of people and walked to my designated seat on the train.

The train begins to move right away. Outside the window, the lights flash by quickly in the darkness.

By tomorrow morning, the train will surely arrive at Busan Station, I thought about the obvious things. The train car was packed with standing passengers, making it difficult for them to even stand.

In the seat next to me, a young woman, who was appropriately called a beauty, had her eyes closed beautifully and seemed to be thinking about something. In my heart, perhaps because of my youth, having been seated next to a member of the opposite sex, some kind of ripple is about to arise.

The alcohol I had drunk before getting on the train did not make me drunk, and my mind became clear. I busily flipped through the pages of the weekly magazine, my gaze kept shifting from the magazine to the woman.

The train that passed Suwon Station runs with even more speed in the darkness, and the sound of the wheels sliding on the rails is heard gratingly.

In the midst of a strange excitement, I just busily flipped through the pages of the weekly magazine and spoke to the person in the next seat.

"Are you going to Busan?" A transparent word came out of my mouth.

The woman hears the words, turns her gaze, and nods her head towards me.

A few words of conversation go back and forth between the woman and me from that time. But then I was at a loss for words.

No matter how much I thought about it, I couldn't find anything more to say. A certain feeling of regret kept stimulating me.

If the conversation with the woman could continue, I felt that my mind would not be bored while the train was running. So I forced myself to make up more words.

"Our connection will end when this train reaches its final destination, won't it?"

The woman, without the slightest hesitation, answered yes.

But then I was at a loss for words again.

Now, no matter how hard I wracked my brain, I couldn't think of any suitable words. So I ended up saying something rude.

"Before our two's connection ends, may I try to seduce you once?"

After saying it in the moment, I regretted it, wondering if I had said something too frivolous.

The woman, on the contrary, with an unchanged expression, bluntly answered, "Are you confident?", and I was immediately flusttered.

"I don't want to fail."

I hurriedly continued.

Is it my honest answer? The woman and I both laughed after saying our words.

The train passing through Jochiwon runs with even more speed.

The people on the train, perhaps because the night was deep, were almost all dozing. My mouth, too, was closed, unable to find anything more to say.

For about an hour while the train was running to Daejeon, no words came out of my mouth. The train enters Daejeon Station.

Many people get off the train. By the time the train left Daejeon Station, the train was starting to empty, to the point where no standing passengers were visible.

The woman in the next seat had an expression as if she were thinking about something alone.

At that time, a person selling things on the train passed by. I called that person selling things.

I paid for a 2-hop bottle of soju and a dried squid. I immediately tore off the squid leg and put it in my mouth and chewed. I took the cap off the liquor bottle and, with bravado, put it to my mouth and strained.

A tremendous alcoholic energy arose in my body. It felt as if a fire would ignite in my stomach right away. My stomach felt nauseous from the alcohol, and my face flushed. My mind gradually became hazy.

I stretched out my arm and put it over the shoulder of the woman in the next seat. The startled woman's eyes became like a rabbit's, and she protested, asking what I was doing.

I opened my mouth, which smelled of alcohol, and spit out the words, "Now I'm slowly trying to seduce you." At my reckless behavior, the woman was rather quiet.

As the train struggled to climb Chupungnyeong Pass, the two of us, as if we had known each other for a long time, had a conversation without any burden. Leaning against each other, sitting close together, we spent a difficult night.

But as time passed, an unknown feeling of regret arises in my heart.

The expectation that the train would run a little slower made me feel that the train, which passed one station after another, was running too fast.

The connection that had formed at the departure station, up to the final destination, piled up with moments of regret, and in the end, the train arrived at Busan Station.

The people who had been on the train all got up at once and headed for the exit. The two people walked together, shoulder to shoulder, to the station plaza.

In the plaza, a faint morning dawn was breaking. I was the first to bring out the words.

"Is the connection between us two over?"

A look of disappointment seemed to pass over the woman's face, but instead of answering, she smiled and bowed her head at my question.

"It was really fun. Goodbye!"

I ran quickly towards the other side of the street with a large bag in my hand. The woman watched my childish back for a long time.

I went up on the bus that ran in the morning. The inside of the bus was deserted, perhaps because it was early. The bus started to run.

Through the window, my gaze searched for the woman in the direction of the plaza, but the woman's figure was not visible. A feeling of regret, as if I had lost a precious item, arose in my heart. My behavior from a moment ago kept coming to mind.

As the strong light of morning shone on the city, I began to be buried in the whirlpool of reality again. Every time the fishy sea breeze hit my face, the ideals that had dominated my mind began to recede.

Now I was faced with the problem of having to solve the reality of the room problem. My outing, where I didn't have a coat, made the winter feel very cold.

There was no one in this Busan to comfort or help me. All I could do was jump into the problem of reality and face it.





18. "Yushin," The Revolution

Yesterday's events felt like ancient history.

People put on expressions to hide their tension, but a suffocating frustration pressed down on their chests.

My conscience kept feeling as if it were being deceived by someone.

The regime, while spewing terrifying threats with sophisticated methods, did not make absolute promises to the obedient people, and in my heart that had believed in God, a feeling of denial towards the God who would not help us began to arise.

I suppress the solitary impulse to cry out furiously, not knowing the feelings of the people of the world.

While agonizing over this and being chased by life for a few days, I began to hear the unfamiliar term "Yushin" (Revitalization) from the media. I couldn't tell if they were promoting it or simply reporting it, but the pages were being filled with special features.

I was just curious how this "Yushin," an unfamiliar word I was hearing for the first time in my short life, would save us from our expectations.

The people in power, or those who wanted to cling to power, said that we had to have Yushin for our survival, but if it was such a good Yushin, people would find out right away, so I couldn't understand why they were so heatedly and forcibly trying to make people's tired minds understand it.

When I went out on the street, the walls of the entire street were plastered with public notices. Law, law, is this country really faltering because there is no law? Or will it eventually be ruined by this proliferation of laws? In my chest, though I couldn't express it, sadness welled up.

Truly, I hope that the country will prosper and be unified as those people say, but the back of the contents, which no one confidently pledges, piles up as a question in my chest. In my heart, a suspicion arose that the future of the country and the nation was falling into darkness.

I ask myself the questions that arise in my mind again. If I repeat this kind of action, all sorts of imaginations came to mind. The burning passion I had accumulated in my young chest, which I wanted to dedicate to my country and compatriots, was cooling down.

Now, what is the mission I must protect in this land? Truly, if I can become a body that can be for my compatriots, I made a sleepless night, filling the time, to find even an unconventional condition.

Really, unfortunate people...

What is power and what is life that they do not hesitate to trample on their own souls? The sad behavior of not being able to dedicate themselves to the unfortunate compatriots and of turning a deaf ear to all the words of resentment and concern and ignoring the truth, my situation, which has many worries, felt more pitiful than their situation.

The rights of the compatriots, the conscience of the people who do not know how to use them for the compatriots, I had to feel fear, and at the foolish judgment and the actions that were about to ruin even themselves, I had to feel a pity beyond anger.

Furthermore, the statements of support from social organizations and opposition figures published daily in the newspapers were more than enough to make me fall into a sense of futility.

Then one day, comrade S, who was a fellow member of my affiliated political party and the chairman of a nearby local party chapter in Busan, came to see me after a long time. I, who had been living in a gloomy mood, was very happy, and he also greeted me with a happy expression.

We went into a coffee shop and sat together. Before I could even speak, he said that all the opposition figures had issued statements supporting Yushin, so I should also agree.

He said that there would be no point in just staying still, and told me where to go, and behind his strong recommendation, he even made threatening remarks that if I made a mistake, I would be crippled by them.

They were truly shocking and sad words. How could a politician, facing a country that was going wrong, not to mention opposing it, just unconditionally approve? I wondered if this was some kind of thunderbolt out of the blue.

In the end, it seemed that my fellow comrades from the nearby local party chapters had also acted in the line of support for some reason.

The next day's newspaper revealed that several Daejung Party chairmen in the Busan area had made statements of support. I had predicted it, seeing how things were going, but when I actually saw the fact with my own eyes, my heart trembled and a wave of sadness came over me.

In an unbearable sense of futility, I tilted a bottle of soju without any side dishes and shed tears alone. And then I let out a silent cry.

"I am by no means a person born for success or glory. I will only live to follow my mission according to my conscience."

A voice like this still remained in my chest.

Then one day, a test began for me. After finishing work, I went into my regular coffee shop, and an official from a certain agency whom I knew was waiting.

Those people asked me for my opinion on Yushin. I brushed it off, saying I didn't know, but for 3 or 4 days, they persistently came to me and urged me to make a statement of support.

It was truly a difficult position. I wanted to scream and go crazy.

At the same time, whenever I closed my eyes, I could see an image of myself suffering some misfortune. At such times, a sorrowful feeling arose, and I did not want to be unjustly wronged.

The official, whom I knew due to my stubbornness, came to me day after day and forced me to give my support and explained the method. I, being flustered, found it difficult even to make excuses as these days continued.

I said to the other person,

"What meaning would a statement of support from one person like me have? Since you are treating me like a person like this, there is no problem in supporting you, but if people find out, they will jokingly say that Yushin succeeded because they got the support of the ignorant Lee Sam-han."

I couldn't submit the statement of support with my own hands, no matter what.

How can there be hope where there is no truth? I tried to protect my conscience with this feeling.

On that day, too, at the moment of parting, the other person's expression was not good, and threatening words were mixed in, saying that he would give me one more chance, so I should think about it again. At his final proposal, I asked for some time to think and parted with him.

Left alone, no matter how much I thought about it, I could not shake off the thought that the measure of suspending the freedom of the people and weakening the function of the constitution could not be the way to serve the country. And so I make a promise in my heart. That I will never give my support...

Finally, the regime announced that it would put the "Yushin Constitution" to a national referendum and decide on its approval or disapproval.

It was truly a heartbreaking thing. If they were going to do it, they should have just said they would do Yushin, but I don't know why they had to drag the people into it and play along.

And yet, in the matter of approval and disapproval, they did not give an opportunity to the dissenters. In this way, they forcibly tried to obliterate the freedom of the people. A society where only the wicked could succeed was approaching, step by step, for sure.

I was so afraid of the world's affairs that I couldn't say a single word and just burned with anxiety. A young man with hope, where should he go? A despair struck my chest.

The sky was resentful, and I was resentful of my own life. And so now, strong soju became my only friend.

I, who had changed my face to be black from alcohol and my nose to be red, was met with a new challenge from my wife, who was worried about my health.

In the midst of that, the seasons also change accurately, making the trees sprout, and in the spring of 1973, when the sea breeze was warm, I saw the world. In this spring, I was trembling, embracing an unbearable loneliness.






19. A Splendid Marriage Proposal

I was gradually weakening.

I felt a simple desire to lean on someone.

When I got drunk, I realized that my surroundings were empty, and at those times, all sorts of thoughts came to mind.

I wonder if I should just get married at this point, and when I ask my weakened self, a laugh comes out.

My age, over thirty, does not make this thought seem strange.

Strange things begin to happen after that day. Every time I met people around me, marriage proposals came in.

The partners people recommended were all women I had never imagined before.

I am also a man, so getting married and taking a bride felt like a natural thing, but my situation, where I had to go through such a thing, was burdensome even to bring up.

Even so, one day, people who knew me well introduced me to a woman who would be appealing to my circumstances, saying I should at least go on one blind date, whether it worked out or not.

She was a woman with the condition that she would not consider wealth or family background if the man was just smart. And she was the daughter of a family where, if I just got married, the housing problem and the room problem would be guaranteed.

In any case, since the person who stepped up to be the matchmaker was said to be the woman's cousin, it didn't seem like an empty story. In my heart, the saying "at worst, I'll break even" came to mind, and because they urged me so much, I agreed to meet.

The rumor was that the woman was the daughter of a rich man who had graduated from a first-rate university.

I decided to meet at the Bando Hotel coffee shop, which was the largest hotel in Busan at the time, at the appointed time. I picked up my dry-cleaned suit, went to the barbershop, and went out to the meeting place. My appearance looked more dignified than usual, to the point where I was unrecognizable.

Several people came from the woman's side. The seating arrangement, with me alone and several people from the other side, immediately made my mood awkward. Only then did the person who said he would be the matchmaker introduce me and the other person.

The woman on the other side was silent, but the group sitting around the woman asked me various questions. They tried not to miss even a single small word. My mood immediately felt like I was taking a job interview.

Given the conditions, I understood it well enough, but in my heart, the heat and enthusiasm were fading, and especially the woman, who was dressed like a celebrity at a glance, I had the thought that she did not seem like someone who would live a hard life with a penniless person like me.

A good amount of time passed. And yet, the other party's group did not want to let go of the tail of the conversation. At this point, I felt like I had become a plaything for people. In my heart, I changed my submissive attitude and attempted a counterattack.

While answering the other side's question, I quickly caught the tail of the conversation.

"May I ask you something?"

The people on the woman's side closed their mouths. My attitude was dignified. The other side also gave their consent.

"My words may be very rude, but since this is something that needs to be discussed with knowledge."

My gaze looked at the woman and I brought out new words.

"Do you know how to cook?"

"No."

At the woman's dispirited voice, the woman's family becomes flustered.

I threw a second question.

"As for sewing, in short, can you make things like socks?"

The other person's face, unlike her dignified attitude until just a moment ago, was on the verge of tears.

"I don't know."

The woman's family members, whether in retaliation or as an excuse, answered for her.

They said she graduated from the home economics department at a university, so why wouldn't she be able to do it? I, with a clear pronunciation, asked the next question.

"Is it really true that you are the daughter of a rich family?"

With a full smile, now thinking that I had been teasing them, I got up from my seat.

The woman's side just stared at me with a blank look.

I went to the counter and paid for the drinks the group had had. Then I quickly left the hotel. Only then was the woman's side very flustered. The person who was her cousin and had introduced us followed me, calling, "Hyeong, Hyeong" (older brother).

I went into a small food stall in an alley next to the nearby Hyeondae Theater and ordered a drink from the middle-aged woman who seemed to be the owner of the stall. A bottle of soju and a plate of pancakes immediately came out on the table.

The woman's cousin who had followed me sits down in front of my seat. I poured soju into two glasses. I poured the glass of liquor in front of me into my mouth in one breath. My stomach immediately became hot, and the uncomfortable feelings were forgotten.

The woman's cousin pours liquor into my glass and asks a question. What was she like, he asks. I, without hesitation, told him my feelings as they were.

"She doesn't suit me. If I have to give an answer, it might be a wrong calculation, but it was 30 points."

The two people, who had become very awkward, continued to empty the soju bottle.

That evening, in a hazy mind soaked in alcohol, I think about what happened during the day and wonder if my behavior was a bit too much.

A pitiful person. Do you know yourself?

At first, I regretted it with a sense of disappointment. But it was a done deal.

Then, after a few days, another thing that appealed to my taste arises from a different place. The woman I came to know this time was not the daughter of a rich family, but she was a beauty.

Her face and figure, which were good enough to compete in a beauty pageant, shook my heart. To be honest, I was also scared. And yet I met the woman, and the woman followed me.

Her family also secretly tried to hold onto me as a son-in-law. I don't know how many times I heard the woman's father's proposal to at least have an engagement ceremony.

In the end, from this woman too, I gave up on myself. After receiving the engagement proposal, I broke my promise. The reason was that the thought of taking a beauty as my wife and worrying my heart out did not appeal to me.

I laughed at my own behavior. I felt that perhaps because I was shabby and miserable, I was afraid of a good position.

After this incident, my behavior became more and more unrestrained. Whether it was because of the world's affairs, I couldn't overcome the emptiness and loneliness.

As the days went by, I couldn't even understand my own heart. I earnestly wished that someone would just save me.

I felt the greatest loneliness since I was born into the world.

I comforted my mood with a bottle of alcohol without a single day's rest.

Then one day, I was introduced to a woman who said she had a job, from a place I had not expected.

The other person was neither rich nor a beauty. After meeting her once or twice, I didn't feel any burden. The woman didn't guard against me either, and even told me her work phone number.

At this moment, I see myself becoming shameless in front of the woman. I was not the me I thought I was.

When I came to my senses, a fear arose in my conscience. And yet, I couldn't do anything about my changing self.

I drank even in broad daylight, and when I wasn't drunk, I was more empty and lonely and couldn't bear it.

It was one such day. Around the afternoon rush hour, I tried dialing the phone number the woman had given me last time. The call went through right away. The person who answered the phone was that woman. We promised to meet soon.

Even while on the phone, I thought of drinking, so I suggested we meet at a nearby draft beer house. The woman had a 500cc glass, and I had a 1,000cc glass in front of me as we talked.

With alcohol and a woman in front of me, I immediately felt like I was becoming something. I downed the large glass in one gulp. The woman filled my glass with the alcohol from her glass in front of her.

When the glass was empty again, the woman paid for the drinks. I felt a little sorry, but after that moment passed, my mood seemed to improve. Then the woman spoke to me.

She asked if I would see her home. I thought. I put my hand in my pocket. I was worried about how much the fare would be.

Thinking about the distance from Gwangbok-dong to Dongnae, a burden kept growing in my heart. But I had to give an answer.

"If you don't ask me to pay for the fare, I have the courage."

The woman laughed. We got up from the table with empty glasses and came out together.

We stood together on the side of the road to catch an empty car. Passersby glance at us and pass by.

The woman sees an empty car first and stops it. I sat side by side with the woman in the back seat. The taxi cheerfully ran towards Dongnae.

With a slight buzz, I closed my eyelids and dozed off. I opened my eyes at the shock of the car stopping. We had arrived at our destination.

I did not know what my next action would be. The empty taxi let the two people off and left. Now that we had arrived at the woman's village, I thought I should go back. At that time, the woman spoke to me, who was hesitating.

"Isn't it that when you see a woman home, you should see her all the way to the front of her house?" she says.

Since I had never had such an experience in my life, I thought the woman's words were right, and saying I was upholding chivalry, I couldn't say a word and followed the woman's behind into the alley.

The woman's house was in a somewhat secluded place. The dog of that house, knowing that a person was approaching the house, barks loudly. A bright electric light brightly illuminates the front of the house.

The family members of that house came out, calling the woman's name. At this moment, my behavior becomes awkward. As if a hidden secret has been revealed, I became flustered.

The family members of that house, with strange looks, stare at me, whom they are seeing for the first time, and hold onto me, asking me to come inside for a moment.

When the atmosphere becomes like this, I am in a position where I can't help it. Like a fish caught on a hook, even though a fear arises in my heart, I went into the room.

The woman introduced her family. I politely bowed to the man who was said to be the woman's father. And then I made some excuses for myself in front of the family.

In the room, the dinner table was still set, as if they were in the middle of finishing their evening meal. The woman's family members asked me how I had had dinner. I just said I had eaten.

At that time, the woman's father has someone bring alcohol. A side dish of stir-fried chicken and soju were placed on the table. The family members of that house, under the electric light, stared at my face, which was a first meeting.

My tanned face, my reddened nose, my chipped front teeth—the people in the room stealthily steal a glance at everything about me.

The woman's father keeps urging me to drink. I was also quite a drinker, but that old man was also quite a heavy drinker. I gradually got drunk.

The old man, who was getting drunk, asked this and that. How old are you, this prosecutor, he asks, and first asks for my date of birth.

He opens his hand and counts on his fingers. The woman's mother, glancing at my strawberry nose, which was giving off a red light, adds a word.

"Do you like to drink?"

I struggled to keep my eyelids from closing and forced myself to answer.

The atmosphere was such that I couldn't just get up and say I was going because of the conversation.

It was because the woman's father kept creating problems and talking. At those times, I answered easily, even though I knew my situation well.

The old man, after counting on his fingers, bluntly asked me what I thought of his daughter.

I, in my drunken state, to be a little more honest, answered that I was not ready to get married. Then he asks what I do.

I said I didn't have a job and just wandered around being a broker. The old man asked where my lodging was. I told him it was somewhere in Yeongdo and pointed to my sister's house. Only then did the people let me go.

I left that house. The night was late. In my head, as I was leaving that house, the thought that I would not be able to meet this woman anymore came to mind in my heart, which was about to become empty.

I walked to the main road and took a bus to Yeongdo, and as my tension eased, my mind became hazy. I strained not to lose consciousness, worried that I might make a mistake on the bus.

It was only in the morning that I was amazed at myself for having managed to get to my sister's house the previous evening.

The next day, in my absence, the woman's relative, a certain high school teacher, and the woman's younger brother, a high school student, had come to my sister's house to confirm my words.

And the day after that, the woman's mother came to my sister's house and seemed to have said that she wanted me to marry her daughter.

My sister, thinking of me who was past the age of marriage, forgot about my circumstances and, perhaps hoping for some benefit from the fact that she was a female employee of a first-class company, without consulting me, the person involved, went with the woman's mother to a fortune-teller's house who was said to be famous to ask.

The wedding day that the two women decided on was a date that the fortune-teller said was good, so there were less than 15 days left. I wanted to be bold about the actions of the women who had decided without consulting me and without knowing my heart, but I was worried about the very urgent date.

In my possession, as for property, I only had about 50,000 won in cash. So it seems my sister started the whole thing and then wrote a letter to my poor sisters in the countryside to send me to get married.

My sisters, upon receiving the news that their brother, who was known to be smart even in the countryside despite having grown up without parents, was getting married, came down thinking of my circumstances.

The day to send the wedding gifts is three days away, in front of me who is completely unprepared.

My eldest sister, who lived the most difficult life among the siblings and was alone, gave an inexpensive Japanese-made watch, my middle sister gave a gold necklace worth three don, and my older sister gave a platinum ring worth three don, and the wedding gifts were compromised.

My brother, who had taken 120,000 won that had been entrusted to a relative's house, saying he would definitely pay it back this time, and who had been so annoying a month ago, also gave 80,000 won.

I was anxious to try to get the wedding gifts with 80,000 won. There were many sets of clothes that cost more than 50,000 won, so it was not enough to even prepare the formalities with cheap cloth.

I went around the market and, instead of matching the money to the cloth, I matched the cloth to the money, so I had to buy and put in defective goods with flaws.

Even I, with my strong stomach, couldn't hide my sad self while preparing the wedding gifts.

The next day, for the last time, I was with the woman who would be my bride, and I couldn't understand why the price of cosmetics was so expensive. A single set of cosmetics cost over 60,000 won. On that day, I just sent the woman who would be my bride back alone.

The next day, thinking of the wedding day that was approaching the day after, I wandered alone on the streets of the international market, looking around in all directions. My footsteps led me to the middle of the international market.

The side of the road was blocked by the footsteps of people due to the peddlers. There I saw cosmetics displayed on a certain cart. I immediately asked the owner of those goods for the price.

The owner of the cart, when a man asked him one by one how much the woman's cosmetics cost, looked at me strangely but answered. The price was too cheap compared to when I had asked at the shop yesterday.

I asked that person. I asked him to tell me only the things that women must use when they put on makeup. The owner of the cart, perhaps thinking he had met a customer, his attitude immediately changed from a moment ago.

I bought eight pieces of cosmetics, whose names I didn't even know, individually. I had no interest in whether they were real or fake. The price of 7,500 won immediately appealed to me.

And so the wedding gifts were packed. Now, it seemed that all I had to do was go to the wedding hall on a good day.

First, I met with the woman who would be my bride and consulted with her. She told me to get a large wedding hall, as many guests were expected, and left it entirely up to the woman who would be my bride.

The woman, hearing my boast and thinking it was a big deal, went around the city on her own and, after inquiring at the wedding halls, reserved the 3rd floor of the Jeil Wedding Hall in Nampo-dong, which was known for having the most seats and a large hall, and informed me.

Four days before the wedding, I had the invitations printed. I picked up about 400 invitations from the printing shop and divided them in half with the bride's side, about 200 each.

When I was actually faced with the task, I was more flustered than when I had vaguely thought about who I should give these invitations to.

No one could take my place in this pitiful situation.


20. I am getting married

All day long, carrying a bundle of wedding invitations, I had to wander the streets in search of people who would make time for my wedding.

"I am getting married."

Even with a heart that easily became shy, I gathered my strength and held out the wedding invitation in front of them. Every time I did, there were people who looked at my aged face, said congratulations on my getting married, and held my hand.
