My wife had an anxious expression seeing me idle and playing around as my business path was blocked. I too was furious at the unusual situation that had befallen me, but in truth, I could not find a way to solve it.

No matter how much I ran around, there was no one who would sell me goods. The regular customers I had cultivated were also lost when the goods ran out.

The workers, who came to the work site where there was no work, believing only in my actions, cursed only the boatmen, not knowing the details. I gave up even the feeling of resenting anyone.

A month passed, and another month passed, but nothing good happened.

My frustrated chest burned and melted, turning into hostility. The way the world was going was just ridiculous and laughable.

The desire to leave for Seoul again began to arise in me. Feeling that it was my mission to fight against contradiction, I had the thought of going for broke.

It was one such day, about three months after I had stopped doing business. A certain shipowner playfully said, "Shall I bring you some sand?"

From that day, for the sake of my child, my wife, and the working people, I started the business again.

Perhaps because I had been hit hard once, I didn't have any other thoughts. We started working diligently. We began to get even more regular customers than before. Gradually, I began to receive recognition for my sincerity and credit from those around me.

Through my actions, I led the workers who were older than me. To break the affection that formed between us, I did not say a single word of unnecessary conversation all day long.

Unlike when we first met, as time passed, the workers came to trust my actions, and I changed into a nearly perfect businessman. In just a few months, I had financial breathing room again.

On my wife's recommendation, I started a savings installment plan at the bank. And not many months after that, the landholding company of the land where I was doing business notified me that they would sell the land, even if it meant dividing it.

I was at a loss for what to do and became worried again. When I consulted with my wife about this, a new breakthrough began to emerge.

We made a deal with the landholding company, got a sufficient grace period for the final payment, and signed a contract for about 150 pyeong. The land I contracted was on the entrance side, and as it happened, there were about 200 pyeong of state-owned land attached to it, so my business was not affected.

The land title was transferred to our name with borrowed money. Then, using that land as collateral, I took out the installment savings and also cleared my personal debts. In my heart, there was no room to have other thoughts.

In order to protect the assets created by debt, I woke up earlier than others, ran around more diligently, deposited money in the bank when I earned it, and used that savings again when needed. By doing this, it was possible to increase my assets even without having any.

In the summer of 1977, with a loan from my bank savings, I also succeeded in getting my own house with a fairly large garden. I was able to see myself succeeding as a merchant.

The life of a merchant could give me much satisfaction. Even when I had become such a diligent businessman, my close comrades were in and out of prison due to the Emergency Measures.

Because of the bank debt I had incurred, I could no longer get myself out. In my home, another child was born. It was a daughter. This time, I did not feel much burden about the increased family size.

The household was harmonious, and others looked at us with eyes full of wonder and praised us for succeeding. It was the most economically successful year of my life.

I also helped my siblings who were crushed by poverty. I created a job for my older sister's husband under me, and I thought a lot about helping my siblings.

I also bought some rice paddies for my poor sister living in the countryside. In my hometown, the rumor that I had succeeded spread widely. They were truly busy days.

Winter passed and spring came. I set up my personal office at the entrance of Yeongdo Bridge. Many people came to see me. There were people who came for business, and there were also people who came to meet for other matters.

Even while watching myself change day by day like this, in the stories of many people, perhaps due to fate, I began to fall into agony again.

The question of whether to work for the homeland and my fellow countrymen or to turn a blind eye began to turn into agony. It was because I had had many experiences of suffering for the sake of conscience and justice until today.

The affection that I must save my homeland never disappeared from a corner of my heart.

The impulse grows stronger when I see the harsh public sentiment changing day by day or the reality of a society that distances itself from common sense.

I cried out in my heart, thinking whether I should accept or reject the actions of frightening people who have forgotten their conscience.

It was a cry that I must save my conscience. For a valuable action, one cannot just sit and wait, lamenting the world.

As Chuseok passed, in my heart that was heating up, the future of the homeland was more heartbreaking than the faces of my wife or children, and not wanting to make excuses to the young people of the next generation about this situation, I reversed my decision several times.

Even while knowing the election law under the Yushin Constitution, which would result in a government-controlled election, and while picturing the faces of those who would run to become members of the National Assembly trusting only this election law,

the resolve to begin acting to awaken my fellow countrymen to the fact that a dangerous future in this reality was approaching us began to form.

The calendar pages turned quickly. On the walls of the streets, printed warnings and statements on large papers began to be posted.

The time was soon signaling October, and in my heart, I began to feel lonely even before starting the work.

When I think of the conscience that will suffer before power, my previous feelings retreat again. So I reprimanded myself again.

I protected myself with the final words that if you have hesitation, the work is finished. I finally put my resolution into action. I gathered about 10 people around me.

I had the people who came to me grasp the polling stations in the electoral district, the number of voters, and the living conditions of the residents, and began to make plans.

This work also ran into difficulties. Because of the term "pre-election campaigning," a person of my status could not step forward even while watching the actions of others.

In my haste, I sent a letter to Seoul. A few days later, my older acquaintance Gu Jwa-seok and comrade Choi Hee-soo came down from Seoul on the same day. The two of them began to strongly dissuade me from my actions. They advised that in times like these, staying quiet was the best way for me.

In the advice of the two, I felt a true friendship. In truth, I too had been hesitating a lot. If someone had just encouraged me a little more, I would have wanted to give up my action.

But God's will did not want that. My heart was moved once again. Perhaps seeing this side of me, even Gu Jwa-seok and Choi Hee-soo, as if they had no choice, gave me advice and now acted together with me.

People who do not fight against contradiction. I began to do what someone had to do in order to fight those people as well.

Regarding the current election law that an independent candidate must go through, Gu Jwa-seok and Choi Hee-soo, along with me, thought deeply about something. Should we create a new force? Or should we just fight alone in this defenseless state? I sought opinions on these two theories.

People said there was too little time to create a new force.

Then one day, Gu Jwa-seok holds out a single-column article from the newspaper before my eyes. It was an article about the submission of the report of the preparatory committee for the founding of the Gimin Party. I called and was able to find out the contact phone number of the Gimin Party's preparatory committee from the Political Party Division of the National Election Commission.

I made a phone call to the Gimin Party's preparatory committee. After receiving a call from them suggesting we meet after I come up to the capital, I sent Gu Jwa-seok up to Seoul in my place to find out the situation of the Gimin Party. Gu Jwa-seok returned from Seoul in two days.

His story was a considerable comfort to me. There were pastors, there was a priest, and untainted young comrades were responding favorably, and his opinion was that at some point, the conscientious forces of the opposition and the conscientious forces within the existing political parties would join.

Believing only the words that Gu Jwa-seok relayed, I hurried the formalities for the founding of a district party for the sake of a party nomination, which was simply more convenient and better for activities than being an independent.

I submitted the preparatory documents to the relevant agency on the same day and set a date for the district party's founding convention. I had someone reserve a certain theater in Yeongdo for the venue, and I commissioned a printing shop to print publications and posters.

At this, the intelligence section of the local police station immediately came to pick me up. The person in charge there who saw me did not have a good expression. It was the story that they had become annoyed because of my actions.

That afternoon, a call came from the theater, which had been paid and even issued a receipt for the use of the venue. It was a notification that using the venue on that day was impossible. The date was the day after tomorrow, and the posters were up on the streets saying where the venue was, so difficult problems arose.

The theater manager said that the owner was in a difficult position because of us. I went to the police station again. I met the person in charge of political affairs.

I relayed the theater's story and gently persuaded him, asking why I, of all people, had to go through this. I pleaded several times, repeating the same words, saying I would finish it quietly and briefly.

That afternoon, after I returned to my office, a call came from the theater. They said that an understanding had been reached with the police station and that I could use it.

I began to make plans with the comrades around me. It was about mobilizing the audience and the procedure for the founding convention. Since we were rushing things so urgently, worries piled up in my mind about everything.

The day before the convention, three young intellectual patriots from the central party's preparatory committee came to see me to attend the convention. I don't know how the rumor spread, but five dissident comrades who were close to me came down from Seoul to see my convention.

From another party, the Democratic Unification Party, comrade Lee Kyung-sik, the former propaganda director who used to lead the young party members, also attended my convention from Seoul in the capacity of a friend.

On the early morning of October 27, 1978, the sky began to cloud over. After 9 o'clock, it started to drizzle.

At 9:30, surrounded by about 10 guests from out of town, I entered the theater.

The preparations were all done for the 10 o'clock convention, but a chilly air even drifted through the empty theater. I thought how desolate it would be if there were no audience because of the weather, and the empty chairs came into my sight.

When it was almost 10 o'clock, 7 or 8 men entered the theater. Thinking that people were now gathering, I turned my face to look and they were familiar faces from somewhere. The group of people who entered the empty theater speak to me with amused expressions.

It was the question of how many people I thought would come today. Hearing that at that moment, I really became worried. Since the weather is like this, about 200 people will come, won't they? The people who heard my words nod their heads, whether in agreement or denial.

From that time, people began to gather in a line at the entrance of the theater. Not long after, the seats were filled, the aisles were packed, and every available space was filled with the heat of the people, and in the small area of the theater, about 2,500 people in the audience pushed to get inside from outside the theater.

It was something I couldn't have imagined, but the ones who were flustered were the agents who had come for surveillance. Someone must have radioed, because the police station's mobile strike squad was dispatched immediately, and a white patrol car was assigned for my event, and high-ranking police officials came out to organize the traffic.

Inside the theater, the program proceeded. The solemn voice of the master of ceremonies tried to silence the crowd of thousands. Through a simple formality, I was elected chairman.

The people gathered in the theater looked at me and applauded.

24. The Thing I Had to Do

The master of ceremonies introduced me in an excited voice.

Hearing his words, I walked toward the podium in the center. Thousands of eyes followed my expression.

I began to gather the eyes of the people moving with me into my own gaze. And slowly, I opened my mouth to the microphone.

"Looking at the reality our homeland faces today, I have cast aside the dissuasion of those around me, and finding no place to hide my young conscience, knowing the current political situation, I have jumped into this heartless scene where I must offer the happiness of myself and my family and even risk my life to awaken the grievances of those who are being deceived, trusting in God and believing in you all.

To the distinguished guests from home and abroad, and to my fellow party members, who have given a warm applause at this moment to my stubborn action of challenging my own destiny while feeling lonely for not having yet found the whereabouts of justice, I first offer my words of gratitude.

The reason I chose the Gimin Party, a name unheard of until now, and came to found it here is that the existing political parties of this country do not present a sense of mission to the era and the people of that era, focusing only on party interests and their own profits, and also seeing their strange habit of not taking responsibility even when innocent people suffer from contradictions they themselves created, I have joined the side of conscientious people today to correct a reality that seems to be going wrong.

Right now, around me, there are pastors and priests from the church. Also, conscientious people who cannot deceive themselves are striving to create the Gimin Party. We do not covet political power, nor do we covet authority, nor do we covet wealth and honor.

We want true democracy, we want a bright society, and we want hope before our fellow countrymen. Our goal is to fight against the evil men who betray history, who keep deceiving others having forgotten their shame, or who try to protect things that have no value to be expected, and we have clarified our intention to directly connect the nation's conscience to revive a politics that follows the truth.

Respected patriotic citizens!

Any society where conscience cannot be protected is an unhappy society. The question of whether we are living in a happy society or an unhappy society is something each of you knows.

If we are living in an unhappy society, it is only right that the regime that exists in this country and its surroundings should take responsibility for it.

And yet, if those people pretend not to know such things, their actions can only be seen as the actions of people without conscience.

In a word, a society that has departed from common sense is a dangerous society. That is why at this time, many people are clamoring that we must save the country.

However, there are people who do not like to hear this kind of talk. So my family has grown worried, and I have become unable to sleep with my legs stretched out. And yet, what I cannot give up even in danger is my affection for my homeland.

Rather than sending more young consciences to prison, my courage to correct politics, even if it means sacrificing my life, cannot be left to a declaration to abandon my conscience. My future will be decided by your judgment.

Still in this country, there are only words that common sense must be saved and conscience must be protected. If one only leans toward fearing one's own persecution and thinking of one's own comfort, that is an act of living with eyes closed and ears blocked in a fearful world, and this very act is the most foolish of deeds, an act that denies even one's own responsibility for oneself.

Furthermore, it means waiting for the beginning of a life of slavery with a self-imposed yoke. Truly, will abandoning oneself become a means of life or happiness for the future of one's descendants? I cannot help but harbor this question.

My beloved fellow countrymen!

I wish to take this opportunity today to cry out to all the people of this land. I want to ask you to fight against your cowardly selves. That is the way to truly love your neighbor and the way to love your country.

Your bystander-like weakness is the way to sink conscience and justice in this land, and a society where justice and conscience do not exist is one that will forever be submerged in darkness. What use will it be to regret and reflect after some more time has passed and life becomes difficult and unfair things happen?

The phenomenon of today is entirely something the whole nation bears much responsibility for. Because we are not willing to act as masters, we are receiving a just punishment.

The country's livelihood becomes difficult because there are people who just point fingers at those who appeal, saying let's live with more sense.

So, people who are good at lying emerge, and such words give birth to distrust, and each person, holding their own pitiful situation of not being able to trust one another, will have cause to beat their chests and regret.

Now the time has come for us to escape from the weak, era-betraying act of just envying others' success and giving up on ourselves. The time has come to abandon silence to gain one's own hope and freedom.

At this point in time, there is nothing for us to protect for the sake of our country. Only courage, effort, and investment in oneself will be the wait for a great result.

I judge that exercising one's given rights and possessing values of self-judgment is the common sense we must have in this land and our duty to our country.

For you to find your ideals or dreams, it is a time when a challenge to yourself is absolutely necessary. Look at this one example.

The poor people of Switzerland, through their courage in protecting only one truth in a place where conditions were not met, became the nation with the highest income in the world.

England in the West, with its long history, with only its will, with a constitution made of simple laws, has protected the world's number one democracy for a long time without wavering.

The reason we have not been able to solve our reality while learning from history about these surrounding situations and circumstances is because we are shunning talented people and it stems from the people's abandonment of their sense of ownership.

There were those who deceived and those who were deceived. So it is a fact that nothing could be protected.

A society where desire is protected rather than conscience will have a time when it feels that pain itself. In the end, it becomes the saying that you reap what you sow. However, I have clearly presented hope now.

I inform you of the fact that in most countries that have achieved development into politically well-run nations or economically rich countries, trust was first formed among the people of that country, and it arose from the honoring of individual creativity and courage.

What we are inferior to these people in, looking at it mentally or physically, is not much. If so, becoming a rich nation and a powerful country is simple. But the stubbornness of the people who cannot do this is just frightening.

I do not wish to insult anyone in a place like this. The one thing I want to say is that because of my desire to save today's suffering homeland, I have become a worthless husband and a worthless father to my family.

Right now, I have no way to control my anxious heart. I have only challenged myself to find what is lacking.

My dear fellow comrades and seniors!

Please send encouragement and advice for the difficult road ahead, watch over me so that I cannot go down a different path, and with a sincere heart, I offer my plea that I may be able to offer my young conscience to my homeland, and with this, I conclude my greeting today. Thank you."

The people in the theater were excited. Applause and cheers exploded. Even though it was a chilly day, the inside was filled with heat.

There were congratulatory speeches from the central party speakers who attended the event, and my older acquaintance Gu Jwa-seok gave a congratulatory speech in his capacity as a friend.

"A young man tries to offer his life in a harsh world, but there is no place to offer it, so feeling a shame that he could not hold up his face even in death before the patriotic martyrs who gave their lives for the country, and so to comfort myself and to give even a little courage to the conscientious choice of comrade Lee Sam-han today, my family at home held me back, telling me not to go down, but I was stubborn and came here.

Citizens of Busan who have come here today, seeing the passion here of those who still seek conscience and justice, I too have only the feeling of wanting to distinguish right from wrong for the sake of the country.

In our country, there is a proverb that says 'a daughter-in-law's life is three years of hardship.' It is a story passed down meaning one must endure three years of being a deaf-mute, three years of being a mute, and three years of being blind in a daughter-in-law's life.

But these days, the high-ranking people in politics seem to want to make our people live like a daughter-in-law. The other day in the newspaper, a statement was published that the crime of false accusation would be severely punished, and it said that the people were engaging in severe slander and malicious gossip.

Living in a harsh world, such things may happen from time to time, but I don't know why those people so often say such things in the newspapers.

They do not pay attention to how many of our countrymen are crying in a society where silence is forced, and they have never once revealed an intention to investigate whether the rumors that those who wielded power over the people suddenly became rich, amassing fortunes from 1 billion to tens of billions, are true or false.

If they gag the mouths of those who think they are wronged and threaten that facts are not facts, who can the people trust and live by, and I don't know why they are making hungry people live like a daughter-in-law, telling them to keep their conscience for what use.

Also, how long this state will continue, living is more tedious than dying. I came to this place today to push a person with conscience and courage into the political scene for the solution of these problems our society is burdened with.

You who live in Busan know better than I do, but comrade Lee Sam-han is the most outstanding figure in this land who can fight against himself, and since I believe that the path he has walked so far is also impeccable as a man of mission for the countrymen living in this land, I want to repeatedly say to you that I am convinced in my heart of the fact that we must place the cross on such a person for the sake of the regime that has many worries, the weary nation, and the homeland that has had no glory.

I also ask you to give encouragement to comrade Lee Sam-han so that he does not get frustrated fighting against injustice, and to become a whip to yourselves, and I earnestly hope that we can regain common sense in a society where common sense has hidden, seek blessings in a place where blessings have grown distant, and be able to regain the truth before history, and with this, I conclude my congratulatory speech."

The venue, filled with the audience, overflowed with the sound of roaring applause, and excitement and emotion filled people's faces until the master of ceremonies introduced the next speaker. The time passed noon.

The agents dispatched to the location had requested that people who had served time under the Emergency Measures not be allowed to give congratulatory speeches, but I could not refuse the request of comrade Lee Kyung-sik, who had come from Seoul just to see me.

I explained the facts up to now and asked him not to denounce the regime too much.

Comrade Lee Kyung-sik held a post in the Democratic Unification Party at the time. The master of ceremonies introduced comrade Lee Kyung-sik to the audience.

People watch with surprised eyes. He introduced himself slowly and in a clear voice.

"I am Lee Kyung-sik, a member of the Democratic Unification Party.

I went to prison because of something called the Emergency Measures, and I was recently released, and today in Yeongdo, Busan, comrade Lee Sam-han is founding the Gimin Party and making a grand resolution to offer his conscience and courage to the future of our country, and I, this unworthy person, have come here to offer some encouragement.

Dear residents who are near!

For the sake of the country and for your sake, I ask you to become a strength and a guardian for a young conscience like comrade Lee Sam-han so that he can fight for the country, and to act together.

Especially these days, I repeatedly ask you to know the facts of any problem and then act. There are many people who lament that they were deceived after the fact. Wouldn't it be better to prevent a sad event before it happens?

The other day I went to see a prison and met all sorts of people. I came to know a little about the world's sentiment.

If I were to reveal all the facts I heard there, the minds of those who came here would be disturbed, and the position of the police officers who are here would be difficult, so I will choose only the words that must be said.

The fact is that you yourselves must find the leader that the country desires, the leader that you desire."

The congratulatory speech of comrade Lee Kyung-sik pierces the hearts of the people. He raises his voice again.

My heart keeps getting anxious. I sent a message to wrap it up simply.

The founding convention ended with greater success than expected. I was just curious about my own future. Time chases time.

It became November.

Now what am I supposed to think? I have to make some kind of decision, but all sorts of worries and pains torment me. When I look back on myself, creepy thoughts kept following me.

My wife, too, revealed a worried-looking face and pleaded with me to live by being observant. When I came to the office, the people who said they would help me whipped my heart. Someone is this way, someone is that way. When I go home, I hesitate, and when I come out, I fall into a sense of mission that I must do it.

It was one such morning. A phone call from a stranger came to our house. The other side of the phone was looking for me. As we talked, the person who called was the preparatory chairman of the 3rd district party of Busan. Even though it was a call from a person I had never seen before, I felt a sense of gladness from the position of a comrade.

The content of the call was that they were holding a founding convention at a certain wedding hall in Jurye at 1 p.m. today, and it was a call asking me to be sure to attend.

From Seoul, Pastor Gu Du-seo (former president of the Baptist Convention) was said to be attending. I relayed that I would also attend at that time and put down the receiver.

A severe fatigue arose in my body. I felt a fatigue as if my head was heavy and my temples were throbbing, perhaps because of alcohol or because I had thought a lot.

In the morning, I went to my office and gave instructions about my tasks to the people who were there, and at noon, I departed from my office to attend the founding convention of the 3rd district party of Busan.

The car I was in found the convention hall, a building on the roadside, without difficulty. At the small wedding hall, the site of the founding convention, several plainclothes police officers were already visible.

I grabbed a guide who seemed to be working for the convention hall there and presented my business card, and immediately a middle-aged gentleman who looked quite old came and greeted me.

That person introduced himself first, saying he was the preparatory chairman who was organizing today's convention. I shook hands with that person for the first time. Pastor Gu from Seoul was also a stranger to me, but upon meeting me, he showed a very pleased expression.

The preparatory chairman guided me and Pastor Gu to the seats set up in the center. Pastor Gu sat in the seat next to me. I expressed my concern to the veteran pastor, who had left his church for the sake of conscience, with stories about the state of affairs and about people with conscience.

Pastor Gu, who had a heroic air, encourages me, saying that God will protect us. At that time, perhaps because the time had come, the master of ceremonies organizes the hall.

The preparatory chairman came to me and made a request. He asked me to give a congratulatory speech. I was flustered because I had not prepared any words, but I answered that I would. In my head, I began to search for the content of the congratulatory speech I would give shortly, what I would say.

The master of ceremonies proceeded with the convention according to the order of events. After the formalities, Mr. Son Yong-gyu was elected chairman. Looking at the appearance of the man who was said to have worked in the teaching profession for a long time, I become worried when I think of today's harsh generation rather than his career. The order of events proceeded quickly.

After the chairman's greeting and Pastor Gu's congratulatory speech, the master of ceremonies introduced me to the audience. I got up from my seat. I walked to the central podium. The gazes of the people gathered there hold me.

I put my mouth to the microphone and raised my voice calmly.

"In a harsh world where it is difficult even to have a chance to look after oneself, because there is a heart that loves the country and loves our fellow countrymen, I convey my intentions with a grateful heart as a comrade walking the same path for the patriotic conscience of Chairman Son Yong-gyu, who created this event today and came out here, and I offer my warm words of thanks for the enthusiasm of the fellow party members who helped make this start today.

In a scene where one feels that something is going wrong, for the reason that someone must jump into this place, confirm the facts, and plant hope, I have consented to my own sacrifice for my simple conscience, but the harsh sentiment of the world is planting fear and loneliness in the effort to find justice.

One has the will but cannot speak, one knows but cannot act. Right around us, the Emergency Measures have been proclaimed.

When I think of my family, I had to grieve for myself, born in this land. People who are afraid of themselves do not try to side with others.

Pain continues on to pain, but there is no one who says they will treat it. So, to try to solve this desperate problem, to fix this ailing society, to do politics, Chairman Son Yong-gyu has come out to this place.

Fellow party members and distinguished guests who have joined us in this place!

I earnestly ask you to widely publicize the fact that Chairman Son is trying to take on the work that you should be doing, and to help him materially and spiritually to become a force to set the politics of this country right.

I saw Chairman Son for the first time in this place today, but looking at his physiognomy, he was completely genuine.

There are many fakes in the world. Everyone, if you think about it, you will remember many. In Mr. Lee's world, it belongs to Mr. Lee; in Mr. Yoon's world, it belongs to Mr. Yoon; in Mr. Park's world, it belongs to Mr. Park; and in the next world, it will belong to the next person; there are many people without principles.

You must know the fact that those who deceive their neighbors, deceive society, deceive others by any means necessary, and grab onto connections, are the ones who are ruining our generation today.

If you pick someone as a worker, they don't work but only try to flatter the supervisor to look good. Is this a worker? It's a courtesan."

Applause and laughter make the hall clamorous. I silenced the audience again with my next words.

"If the farming is ruined, the blame is placed on the heavens. The one who was deceived cannot even speak. In this world, for that reason, there are many excuses.

In simple terms, let me ask you one thing. In Article 1 of the Constitution of the Republic of Korea, there is a clause that says sovereignty resides in the people. You know what this means, right? It means that you are the masters of this country.

Everyone, then, have you ever been treated as masters? If you get on the wrong side, you won't even be treated as a nuisance. Why has the world turned into such a kaleidoscope?

It is because of the spineless characters; it is because of the people who forget their duties and neglect their responsibilities.

So, frustrated people can't stand it and, trusting only in their patriotism, cast aside the dissuasion of their families and, leaving aside financial ruin, have jumped into a place like this where they must even risk their lives. It must be set right. It must be set right. With that heart.

Even at this very moment, in my house, there are only sighs. They say my wife is on the verge of death because she is so anxious about my actions.

Have you ever listened to the plea of a woman who tries to persuade me, asking what is a fellow countryman and what is a homeland, a woman raising a child who cries out to live like others?

In the heart of a person who is not made of wood and stone, there are times when the heart melts. Every time I see the pitiful tears of my child, I feel the plea of a worthless father.

But on the other hand, with the single mind that I will protect my conscience, I am stubbornly enduring. We will offer our conscience to this land. No matter what difficulties there may be, we will not disappoint the people who love us.

Fellow party members and distinguished guests who have come here today!

I earnestly ask you to deeply understand Chairman Son's situation and feelings, and even if there are shortcomings, to be mindful that he is a person with conscience in this land, and to guide and whip him on.

There is a truth in the proverb 'A baby grows up to be an adult.' Now, while nurturing hope, let's pledge together to become a wise people, and with this, I conclude my congratulatory speech at this ceremony today. Thank you."

The sound of applause in the hall washes away the ringing in my head.

Someone in front of me hinted that when I was speaking, a spasm occurred on the faces of people who looked like government agents. I left the hall with Pastor Gu.

Chairman Son Yong-gyu ran up to the side of the two of us. I was about to just leave, but Chairman Son urges me to at least have a meal together before I go. There were about 10 executive members of the 3rd district party of Busan and aspiring organizers of other district parties.

We ordered lunch at a certain restaurant in Eomgung-dong, and after the meal was over, the group dispersed.

Chairman Son, along with his wife, came along to see Pastor Gu Du-seo off to my office at the entrance of Yeongdo Bridge. I ordered a cup of tea for each of them and sent them off.

Watching the busy schedule chased by time, I think that today is passing by again. In my heart, the sense of burden grows even larger.

To be honest, my heart was wavering. It was because the temptation of stability kept stimulating my heart. And yet, I had a separate destiny that was set for me.

This destiny was something I could do nothing about. I spend one night with this thought and that. Whenever I woke up from sleep, my head ached. The telephone bell rang loudly.

Who would be calling so early in the morning? While thinking, I picked up the receiver. A certain ominous premonition flashes through my head. The person who called me was the wife of Mr. Son Yong-gyu, the chairman of the 3rd district party of Busan who had held the founding convention yesterday.

The hoarse voice that immediately flowed from the receiver suggested that something unusual had happened. She said that last night, in the middle of the night, some strangers came to the house and took him away, and there has been no news.

Her worried voice, asking what she should do, kept weighing on my mind. In any case, there was no way to know for now. I ended the call by putting down the receiver with only the answer that I would look into it.

After eating breakfast, I went to my office and around 10 o'clock, I called the person in charge of political affairs at the police bureau and asked.

I told them I had received a report that Mr. Son Yong-gyu was missing and asked if it was their jurisdiction.

But the story from that side was that he was being held at the Bukbu Police Station, and they even added another remark that the speech I had given yesterday had passed without incident.

My mind is dumbfounded and falls into a state of collapse. I pushed aside my busy schedule and ran to the Bukbu Police Station, thinking I should at least find out the situation.

I went to see the chief of the intelligence section and, revealing my identity, asked what was going on, and he said that this matter was not under their jurisdiction and they were just waiting for instructions from above. At that time, a certain detective brought in Chairman Son.

Upon seeing me, Chairman Son gives an abashed smile, yet acts innocently as if he has some expectation. I could not disappoint his heart.

I reassured him for a brief moment with the vague words that he would be released soon, and then told the detectives the unnecessary words of "please take good care of him," and came out.

Outside the police station, Chairman Son's wife and a close associate of his, who had been there for a while, were standing helplessly in front of the main gate.

I said that it seemed things had gone wrong, as I told them the truth, but since the matter was not yet finalized and they were waiting for instructions from somewhere, a matter of this extent would probably turn out well, giving them vague words. And as I came back, all sorts of thoughts came to my mind.

The pitiful image of the wife, whose face was bright just yesterday, now standing with a dark face, stamping her feet in front of the police station, would not be erased.

The thought comes to mind that if something happened to me, my wife would be loitering around like that. I also felt like I could understand a woman's heart regarding my wife's seemingly causeless complaints about why I couldn't live like others. I look back on myself.

When I think of my formative years, being treated with contempt since birth, scorned by neighbors, even abused by my siblings, and having protected my life like an animal, and now thinking that I am bringing upon myself persecution from the regime, I wanted to wail at my own fate.

What does God want to happen to me? While holding onto the pain I receive because of my conscience and sense of justice, and the greater pain of not even being able to talk about that pain to anyone, I informed the party in Seoul by phone about the events happening in Busan.

This was the entirety of the actions I could take regarding the matters around me.

I feel pathetic. How can I do anything like this? While having the conditions to enjoy myself like others, there were times when I really disliked my own actions, why I was trying to run into danger.

Hesitating whether to confront or retreat, even after founding the district party, I had neglected the registration process for over 10 days without taking any action.

After November 10th, pressing phone calls came relentlessly from Seoul. They were asking me to prepare and send the district party registration documents.

Only then did I finally make a decision. I had the party members who were helping me, about 20 of them, get their membership application forms and certificates of seal impression. But as expected, even after two days, only about 30 membership applications and seal certificates had come in.

As the rumor spread that the Gimin Party, which had emerged crying out for justice, was a group of conscientious forces, people who had been so worn out by the world seemed to be turning a blind eye altogether, perhaps in case something might happen.

I had to laugh. The imminent deadline weighed on my mind. Now it was my turn to step up myself.

I had the district party's secretary-general, comrade Kim, prepare the registration documents by noon the next day.

The next morning, at 9 o'clock, about 40 people gathered in front of the Sinseon 2-dong office. The young lady in charge of civil affairs was sweating. We had processed the receipt of about 40 membership applications and seal certificates without much difficulty.

My comrades and the district party secretary-general looked at me with eyes full of wonder.

On the afternoon of the 13th, the clerk who had taken the registration documents to the election commission came back late that day with the registration certificate. We had accomplished something no one could have guaranteed.

On the 15th, a message came from the central party that they would hold the founding convention. I hurried busily for the event that was approaching the next day.

On the morning of the 14th, with two comrades, I drove towards Seoul in my passenger car. The car was able to reach the front of Nakwon Arcade in Seoul only around 4 p.m.

The office of the preparatory committee, which I was visiting for the first time, was full of people. A certain comrade who had attended my district party's founding convention recognized my face and, welcoming me very much, introduces me to the various people. The surrounding eyes observe me. I quickly become busy shaking hands.

I waited for the moment when the surroundings quieted down and then handed over the envelope containing a copy of the district party registration documents from my document envelope to the organizing committee.

Only then, because of my personal situation, I just heard the schedule of the event and came out of the office bustling with people. Leaving behind the words that I would contact them when I got a place to stay, I headed towards my car where my two comrades were waiting.

A short while later, I got a room at the Century Hotel on Cheonggyecheon, a place close to the preparatory committee's office, and told the two comrades who had followed me to take care of their business in Seoul if they had any and to come by 8 a.m. the next morning.

As the two comrades left the room, I immediately felt fatigue all over my body. I notified the preparatory committee's office of my hotel room's phone number and, having come up to Seoul after a long time, I thought of an old comrade and picked up the phone. Some people's phones didn't connect, and from another side, they said they were glad to hear from me and rushed over right away.

I exchange drinks with the people who came holding soju bottles and dried squid legs, seeing their faces that treated me as frankly as in the old days. The night deepened. The effect of the alcohol rises to my face. One by one, two by two, they leave the hotel to catch the last city bus.

I got into bed, mulling over the words of comfort left behind by my old comrades as they departed. As I closed my eyes, fatigue immediately rushed in.

At that moment, the telephone bell rings. The ringing didn't stop and kept coming. My mind is about to get irritated because of the alcohol. I forced myself to pick up the receiver.

The other side asks for me first. I answered. The voice from the other side of the phone immediately changes to a pleased one. The person who called was a graduate of a theological college and a preparatory priest of the Catholic Church.

It was a call asking for my approval as they were going to elect me to the political committee at tomorrow's founding convention. I mumbled something noncommittal and put down the receiver.

When I woke from my sleep, it was morning, and the two comrades had returned to the hotel. After roughly getting myself ready, we set off towards nearby Nakwon-dong.

The preparatory committee's office was chaotic. I still didn't know the location of the founding convention. Curiosity is triggered. I grabbed the person in charge of organization for the preparatory committee and asked with an abashed face where on earth the convention was being held today.

After hesitating for a good while, he told me the fact that they hadn't been able to decide on a location until now. It was a pitiful excuse that there was no way to get one even if they paid money.

Only after a long while did people rush about busily. They said they had decided on a place at a Presbyterian church in a place called Teobatgol on the outskirts of Seoul.

The cars started moving. My car's driver, who was unfamiliar with the geography of Seoul, struggles to follow the car in front. Even at this moment, I began to feel the heartlessness of the people on the other side of reality.

If they do this for such a small matter, what will they do for the next? My future kept weighing on my mind as I thought about the next things I would have to face, which were not one or two.

The car had come to the outskirts, and yet it crosses over a mountain village. After that, it stopped at the place where the church was. And there too, trouble arises before we even start the event.

I don't know how they found out, but the message that came down from the upper echelons of the affiliated church was the pressure that a political gathering should not be held inside the church. Now, only the decision of that church's pastor remained.

The pastor, rather, felt sorry for our side and told us to use the lower basement area.

The central party's founding convention of a political party was to be held in a basement with a vinyl floor.

It was a moment when a resolution burning with conscience and a sense of justice was proceeding amidst harsh public sentiment and threats laced with fear. As the order of events proceeded, the party leadership was formed, and 12 political committee members were elected.

The convention hall, despite the chilly weather, was filled with heat and was led smoothly to the closing ceremony. The faces of all who conducted the convention were solemn, for what reason of resolve I do not know. "Fear not, fear not," a powerful hymn spreads out into the space. The convention had ended smoothly.

The executive board notifies that the representative supreme council member and the 12 political affairs committee members should not return home if they live in the provinces, but should go to the Nakwon-dong party headquarters and wait, in order to discuss the issues left today.

I walked with my group toward my car. Inside the car, a strange man was already sitting in the passenger seat.

More than the suspicion of how he had picked the lock and was sitting there, my future path becomes more and more uncertain. I asked for the understanding of the person who had asked for a ride in my car and began to drive towards the city.

The gutsy man sitting next to the driver's seat does not introduce himself and does not open his mouth for a single word. Even when my car finally arrived at the destination in Nakwon-dong and stopped, the man did not try to get out of the car.

I went into the party headquarters. I did not tell anyone the story of what I was currently experiencing.

At the central party office, they said they would soon hold a political committee meeting, and the place they guided us to was a spacious Korean-style room in a nearby hotel. In the center of the room, a table was prepared, and thirteen cushions greeted us.

Among the 12 political committee members, I was the youngest in age, but it seemed I had the most political experience. During the reopening of the meeting, I could not say anything here. And yet, the meeting was proceeding based on my remarks.

I chose a method to end the meeting simply and proposed the opinion that all agenda items be postponed until after the general election, and it was passed. I had the meeting end without a clash of opinions by putting forth the condition of approving only a few working-level staff who could organize the party and recruiting more capable talent.

That evening, at the invitation of Chairman Lim Chang-jin of the Dobong district party (who was a young entrepreneur) who had not been given any key post at the founding convention, to have dinner with the political committee members, I made a proposal and we accepted.

Around 6 p.m., we each got up from our seats. I walked to where my car was. Until then, the strange man was stubbornly sitting in the passenger seat.

I told the comrades who had come up with me from Busan that our business was now finished and we were departing for Busan, and at that, the man who had been sitting like a stone statue in the passenger seat of the car gets up from his seat and comes out of the car.

And for the first time, he opens his mouth and greets me. He says "Go safely" and even extends his hand to ask for a handshake. I had the driver drive the car for a while.

And then I got an inn nearby with a garage. I ordered dinner for the two comrades and I ran to the dinner party.

At the invited table, besides the party's political committee members, district party chairman-level figures whom I thought had left for the provinces were also present, so there were about 20 people in the room.

In my heart, I felt awkward as they were people I had met for the first time through this event, but I also felt a curiosity about what kind of people they were.

At first, the atmosphere was awkward, but as alcohol was served and drinks were passed around, and a slight tipsiness came over us, people try to relax.

Someone made this suggestion. That we go around and introduce ourselves and our history. Everyone agrees. One by one, they give their self-introductions splendidly. To my ears, they all seemed to be excellent figures. After an introduction ended, eyes full of wonder and applause came out.

An atmosphere was waiting where I had to talk about my not-so-proud past. Then, my turn came, the second to last.

My mind was shaken by the alcohol I had drunk as it was given. The people in that place were watching me.

A dignified attitude for my young age, so perhaps people were more curious about me. I stood up from my seat and slowly began to open my mouth.

"My father was a stonemason who cultivated a slash-and-burn field. I have not seen my father's face.

I heard that he passed away shortly after I was born, when I cannot hold it in my memory. I was raised by the hand of my widowed mother.

My mother could not love me. Because I had become a burden on the strength of a weary woman.

She too passed away when I was nine.

From the age of ten, I came to confirm the sentiment of the world. Trying to live in a cold society, I am a man who has experienced all sorts of things.

My shabby appearance was scorned by the neighbors. Sometimes I was the target for the ill-tempered children in the village to vent their anger. Even my siblings abused me. I have lived fearing the world like a powerless animal.

At the age of 13, I was a newspaper boy, an ice cream seller, a worker at a Chinese-owned foundry, anyway, I have tried any kind of menial work.

Right now, I cannot introduce all of my complex self. Because it's too long. I went to a place called the army, and when I was discharged, I had become an adult.

Because of the problem of bread, I tried to get a job, but because I had no guarantor, I couldn't get a job several times, and on a day when I felt like I was suffocating, I felt some mission in the world and ran around saying I would try politics. I finally felt that it suited my aptitude.

When I entered an organization, I was treated like a human being for the first time in my life. I joined the Daejung Party and have served as a district party chairman, youth bureau chief, social organization chairman, and preparatory committee chairman more than ten times.

When I, who had become bold, ran in the election on May 25, 1971, the people who knew me were agape. Because of my own ignorance, I always needed a staff officer, and I have never once sat in a position with the character 'vice' attached to it.

This time, I thought I would try to be the party representative, but I only became a political committee member, but I feel the attraction that the place we are in is a conscientious force and I expect my own development through my conscience. Let's get to know each other well from now on. Thank you for giving me the opportunity to introduce myself."

The crowd was solemn at my introduction, which was delivered in a speech-like tone. This time too, eyes full of wonder are directed towards me.

The next person also got up from his seat and introduced himself. We were able to roughly grasp the backgrounds of the figures in the crowd.

Feeling quite full, I was the first to get up from my seat and ask for their understanding. Pastor Gu gets up from his seat, saying let's go together.

Mr. Lim Chang-jin, who had hosted the dinner, follows us to the door and urges us to take his car. I, who was not shy, agreed and got into the car first, then urged Pastor Gu to get in. The car passed by my nearby lodging, which was a short distance away, and sped towards Pastor Gu's next destination.

For some reason, a worry began to arise in my heart. The work we have to do together from now on is no ordinary matter.

I was curious whether the regime would first condone the normal start of the party.

If they do not condone our conscience, our fate will meet with misfortune before we can even act.

I thought of a bird trapped in a cage. Its situation of wanting to fly in the open air but being unable to fly is clearly visible.

The question arises whether justice can stop a bullet. If things go wrong, the frightening thought of having to abuse myself with a frustrated and anxious heart does not leave me.

The day broke while I was in a state between sleeping and not. I left Seoul with the two comrades.

The car running on the highway sped towards Busan, and on the afternoon of the 16th, I returned to my office.

The two comrades who had accompanied me to Seoul informed the other comrades gathered in the office of the fact that I had become a political committee member of the central party. The people here begin to trust me again. Worries and concerns do not want to leave my mind.

As time went on, I was able to confirm this feeling even more. When I called to inquire whether the central party had been officially registered, the organization department of the central party just stalled for time, saying it would be done tomorrow, the day after tomorrow.

There was a big difference in saving the 2 million won deposit and in the activities of the campaign workers if the party was registered. The notification came only after the 23rd had passed, the day the registration's effect would have been generated if the party had been registered.

It was a sad notification that it was utterly impossible. I don't know how tediously I hesitated and spent the 24th. But I had greeted the morning of the 25th again.

Fate could only be decided by time. A fierce conflict began in my heart.

Should I go out or sit down? I wished time would go by a little faster, but I don't know why time is so long on this day.

Several people around me are watching my final decision.


25. A Difficult Decision

In just a few hours, the 고민 (agony/indecision) could be resolved. With not even a pretext for an excuse, the time was so tedious I couldn't bear it.

The people around me, who had been watching my actions and just observing my situation, began to incite me. At that moment, the office manager, comrade Kim, as if sensing my hesitation, pressed me, asking if I was going to let the time pass.

Feeling like I was dying, I gave an unavoidable answer to the people waiting for a decision. Fate was determined not to let me escape from a difficult situation.

With the last two hours left before the registration deadline, I gave my seal to the office manager and called home to have a 5 million won certified check issued. Vitality began to surge in the faces of the people who had been tediously just watching my situation.

The office manager gathered the documents he had prepared. A few people followed behind him. A little while later, the people who returned to the office placed the candidate registration receipt on my desk. Whatever the circumstances, my mind immediately grew busy. I forced myself to find strength.

But before me, the things that were to come rose up, fearful and agonizing. In any case, I could not back down now. For me, who knew the reality, I considered my action to be the greatest means among the actions of offering one's worth to the homeland.

I don't know how much I felt like a foolish idiot, confronting a figure behind the power at this point in time with only conscience and courage. Even in that state of mind, for the sake of the courage of the next generation, I began an action that was perilous beyond compare.

I forced myself to chase away the agonizing thoughts, tracing the apparitions of my child, my wife, and the people who cherished me that rose before my eyes.

Even while thinking of the retaliation or aftereffects that would come after the election, I was resolving to steadfastly keep my convictions as a candidate for the National Assembly. I hurried, urging the people next to me with the tasks I had to do one by one.

I ordered a banner and wrote the manuscript for the election bulletin with my own hands. Yesterday and today became different. Time flew by incredibly fast. My head was constantly filled with all sorts of things I had to figure out.

I had to immediately find campaign workers for each neighborhood and also had to formulate the text for the speech I would carry to the joint speech rally. For me, sleep was always scarce. The financial situation was also an immediate worry. The handicap of being an independent was losing its nerve amidst the repeated stern warnings from the authorities.

As soon as I opened my eyes, my temples throbbed and my head was heavy. It seemed the expression 'helpless' was created for situations like this. When I thought about it, there was nowhere to lean on for support. In this dreadful situation, the only thought I could have was to place a vague hope in the joint speech rally.

November 28, 1978, was a winter day, yet rain was sprinkling from the sky. That very day was the first day the joint speech rallies were held. But in the afternoon, the rain stopped and the weather cleared. From then on, the temperature suddenly dropped.

When the time came and I went out to the speech venue, the Cheonghak Elementary School playground, a sense of panic I hadn't felt before kept arising, and my head was distracted with strange thoughts. Worry and fatigue piled up. My body, as if feeling the cold, trembled unusually.

At that time, an announcement was coming from the speaker installed on the playground. They said they would be drawing for the speech order, so if a candidate did not come out quickly, they would consider them to have withdrawn and proceed with the draw; the people making the announcement spoke matter-of-factly from the beginning.

From my group, the office manager took my seal and went toward the place where the microphone was installed. A little while later, the person who had drawn the lot came back with a slightly embarrassed face and told me it was number 10.

Considering the weather and the time, I was worried. The thought arose that perhaps I would end up giving a speech to an empty playground.

For me, my turn came around the time the winter sun was hanging on the western mountain. The microphone from the election commission called my name. Contrary to my once confident thoughts, I went up to the podium with a fearful heart.

The cold feels even colder because of the temperature. Remembering the allotted time, I opened my mouth towards the wide playground.

"I am Lee Sam-han, who has come here to give the 10th speech with the 10th ballot number in the 10th general election."

I said, and bowed my head. The people, as if in return for my greeting, applauded. I opened my mouth, thinking of my next words.

"To have placed the cross on one person three times in this regional election is not my magic but will be the will of God. To repay all of you who have waited in the cold weather, I will first tell you why I came to run for the National Assembly.

There are many frustrating things in my heart. There are people who do politics, but there is no politics around us.

If you sit still and listen, there are many patriots, but in reality, the state of the country is a mess. The people really have very little to believe in.

I came to think that the place where the most people in the world live who have been defrauded and beat their chests in grievance is the land we live on.

So, I was curious why this world, as it goes on, is not getting better but worse, and I had to find out what on earth the members of the National Assembly we elected did when they went to the National Assembly that so many aggrieved and sad people have come to exist, and also to reflect the circumstances around us that cannot be neglected, I have come before you to run in this quite difficult election.

I am not someone who came out to gain fame because I have a lot of money like other people. Nor is it that I have a good career and want to boast. Nor am I a person who came out to teach someone because I have a good academic background.

Unable to stand and endure the state of the world that I simply cannot bear to watch and the worrisome future of the country, knowing that a person like me coming out in a world like this is not right, yet my young conscience could not just turn a blind eye to the homeland, so to save the country, to save the dying politics, I raised a precious sum of money, and though you'll know when you actually see it, for someone like me the deposit will become a donation, but I came out having put down 5 million won.

Because this election is an important one for the country and for us as individuals in our future lives, my resolve was also not like others and was particularly great.

In this important election, I ask you, the sovereign citizens of this land, not to be deceived by personal acquaintance, the temptation of material things, or threats and appeasement, but to participate as if you were a candidate yourself, even if you did not register as a candidate, and I must, as a citizen with a conscience, ask you to work together to save the future of the country by fostering an election climate where you tell those around you that this election is an important one, and that you must find for yourselves a person who can work for the country, a person with courage, a person with conscience, a person who can bring justice to life.

Voters who have stayed behind to listen to the speeches until the last person, even though the weather is chilly because the temperature suddenly dropped today,

Even if I don't hear your words, I think I can fathom your hearts. My heart, too, right now, even though I am out here giving a speech, my actual feeling is exactly the same as your feelings.

I will promise to fight against the contradictory politics of today that does not protect law and conscience.

I will fight against the incompetent and cowardly pseudo-politicians who turn a blind eye to justice. For that very reason, I came out to this place today. Everyone, those of you who think that guy is a decent guy, please give some applause. Today the weather is cold, perhaps that's why my heart is cold."

As I finished speaking, laughter and applause erupted from the crowd. I brought out my next words.

"Looking at the world these days, everything I see is just dumbfounding and frustrating. They put handcuffs on other people's consciences with things like Emergency Measures, and when I see them squandering money borrowed from outside, let alone saving what they've earned, and people prattling on without principle that this is good politics and making those people leaders, it even brings tears to my eyes.

A society where talented people are not protected by that society, this kind of thing is not even in the history books. What will happen if sincere people worry about people who have abandoned their conscience?

There are people who have amassed tens of billions of won without ever doing business once. They are goblin millionaires. I am curious if this phenomenon is the magic of a club or if it is the magic of swindling. In truth, people who do not know envy the lives of those people. And because of that, there are all sorts of things in the world.

It is an undeniable principle that many wronged people will emerge, but when I see these wronged people beating their chests with nowhere to appeal, that pain is resonating in the powerless chest of one who has a conscience.

To end these sad stories, I have run for office to show the principle that all of our countrymen must struggle with their cowardly selves.

Among those who have come here, there are few whose circumstances are worse than mine. As long as you do not show your actions for your country, is there any need to foresee that our future will be buried in darkness?

Even if everyone makes excuses that they cannot take responsibility, in the near future, we will suffer damage that will be difficult for us to recover from by ourselves.

I cannot be a bystander to this. I was born in this land and have experienced enough hardship, more than anyone. Each time, I have lived until today with hope for the future.

Now that future is in danger. The ones who can save it are you and I. Will you do it? Shall I do it? Whoever does it, it is something we must tackle with firm resolve.

Even at this very moment, among my rival candidates, there may be some who do not understand what I am talking about. For those people too, I will say a word.

Especially those who have been around politics and government circles have probably reflected their opinions a lot in the meantime.

But looking at the state of the country these days, it's this shape and this form. I would like to ask those people, if they have even a little conscience left, not to bother trying to think of excuses for today's society, but to make a courageous decision for a new era.

And to the others, it is also my assertion that this place should not be made into a place that turns into something like a speech contest venue.

I will warn you that this is not an era where the act of blocking the path of a talented person who wants to save the country becomes a source of pride in your hearts. I will propose that those who feel they cannot lay down their lives to solve the current difficult problems, I'm sorry, but please withdraw from this place today.

The country is important, hope is important, and truth is important; that is the reality we must see today. I confidently pledge to you, the candidates and voters, that I will do this work.

As a person who has always respected the parliamentary activities of our country's politicians Kim Doo-han and Seo Min-ho, I will promise to walk the same path as them."

At that moment, the bell signaling the time rang.

I continued with my final plea.

"Everyone, when you return to your neighborhoods today, please convey my words. I will promise to not only bring honor to our region but also to illuminate the future of our country. Thank you."

My speech ended. Even the applause squads of other candidates clapped. The last speaker in the order went up to the podium over which the sun had set.

On the playground podium where dusk was falling, the last person's speech ended on time. I, with a body and mind that had become a complete wreck, began a difficult march.

Worries and regrettable problems grew more and more numerous. Because of my position as an independent, my movements were back and forth between my home and the campaign office. Trying to abide by the strict election law, I could not even visit people I knew.

A bird in a cage had no other way but to ask for sympathy from the people on the outside with its expression.

All sorts of people came to the campaign office. Most of them, in the end, frankly demanded to exchange votes for money. At the desperate scene, my heart was sore and pained.

The election method felt like a government-controlled election, and there were many voters who did not want to think about tomorrow's reality. While thinking about how many difficulties this country would have to go through in the future, I held on for the 1% hope rather than the 99% impossibility.

The judiciary and the executive branch frequently posted papers with warnings that they would severely punish election law violators on the streets.

My own appearance, participating in the election without any backing in the world's strictest election law and asserting my own claims, was also comical. Most of the candidates just did the P.R. for the flawed government and only received applause from the voters.

I protested to myself, asking if this was an election, but there was no way an answer would come. In this frustrating state of mind, the second joint speech rally was held at Bongnae Elementary School in Yeongju-dong.

The weather was clear and the climate had softened and was warm. The crowd filled the small school's playground. My speech order was fifth. After listening to the four speeches, my turn came. I went up to the podium.

Perhaps because I had been under too much stress and spoken a lot in the meantime, my throat was completely hoarse, and my frustration reached its peak.

The crowd applauds, urging me on with my speech. I slowly put in effort, cleared my throat, and opened my mouth.

"At the speech rally at Cheonghak Elementary School the day before yesterday, I gave the tenth speech. Waiting for my turn, I got to hear nine speeches.

All of them, just like speakers at a speech contest in elementary school, only said things that seemed to curry favor with the people in power today, like a spokesperson for the Yushin government, telling people to endure without any alternative,

and while telling thirsty people, they leave out when the rain will come and just go on about superficial things, and when I saw them having the people they brought, having paid them a daily wage, just clap, I was so fed up with their speeches that anger welled up in my heart.

At that time, when my turn came, I yelled a bit at the innocent microphone, and now my throat is so hoarse that I believe it will be uncomfortable for you all to listen to my words.

But I too have come up to this stage with an anxious heart, thinking of society and the future of our country, so I ask for your understanding and cooperation for the given time.

My assertion is that we should not just be deceived and elect people who are good at making excuses and only suffer a dirty sight, but I will first make the assertion that we must support and elect a person who can solve the painful and difficult problems we are facing one by one.

My conviction is not to endlessly repeat the tedious work of doing Yushin for generations of our children, and in the midst of insufficient hope, understanding and being deceived by a Korean-style democracy, and being deceived again, and even if it's unfair, closing our mouths and enduring, and enduring again, but to pick a smart and courageous person and try to do a world-class democracy and make a first-class nation.

My political assertion is not to live by believing only the words of a person who speaks well, but to identify the causes of things that don't work one by one and set them right, and to improve the social climate so that frustrated people are not frustrated.

An election is to pick a worker called a member of the National Assembly for a country, but I would like to ask you not to commit the difficult act of picking a person who wants to become a master.

Among the people who came out in this election, among those who came out with the expectation that they only need to be 1st or 2nd thanks to the current election law, it seems there are people who look like they can be 1st or 2nd.

For the reason that even a bad law is law, while carving into my heart the frustration of not being able to speak the truth as it is at a scene where the law is being brandished, I have run for office saying that this country should not be like this, having put down 5 million won, which is a very large sum of money in my life, as a deposit, but there are only frustrating things when it comes to letting you know about myself.

The only guaranteed method of campaigning publicly is the opportunity of 4 joint speeches, but even that is for a short 20 minutes, so if you add up all 4, it's only 80 minutes.

The venue is not chosen at my discretion either; at a designated place, and even there, the ranking is decided by drawing lots for luck, so I am just at a loss.

If I draw badly, I have to appeal my heart-rending patriotism to an empty playground after everyone has left, and even if I draw well, in front of the applause squads brought by rich people and those who hang around power, I have to think of my own situation and cry, so what on earth is the right thing to do about this pitiful man's situation!

Also, some people, knowing that it is an election where you shouldn't spend money, are just spraying money. To explain simply, in a race with 7 people, there are people who are completely free, people with their hands tied, people with their feet tied, and then someone like me is in a situation where I have to abide by all the rules with both my hands and feet tied.

What is this, an obstacle course? Everyone, if you can judge fairly, please check. I am number one.

But it seems this is not an obstacle course. So, out of human greed, aren't other people violating the rules?

The reason is unknown, and if you ask the referee because you don't know the reason, do you know what they say? Their words are even more plausible. It seems like a funny race, doesn't it? This time, they are making a fuss in the newspapers that they will definitely hold a fair election, but is this method a fair election?

I am not making a fuss like this because I think I won't be able to become a member of the National Assembly now. I am crying out because I am frustrated when I think of the country, think of the position of our countrymen, and think of history."

While forcibly maintaining my voice that seemed about to give out, and confirming the difficult scene where even spasms were occurring on my face, as I confessed the facts piled up in my heart to those around me and added strength to turn people's attention to the scene of the facts, applause continuously erupted from the crowd.

When I finished my speech and came outside, a countless crowd surrounded my path. Without understanding the will of the people who were not trying to discern reality correctly, I was doing my utmost for my own suffering and sacrifice.

As the voting day approached, the atmosphere among the people changed. Money was flying around, and even an atmosphere of fear was being created.

In that situation, I only feel the fact that I have nothing to lean on. And yet, the comrades only incited the complaints of the campaign workers, saying that funds must be released. I became worried. And yet, difficult things just kept happening here and there.

A female campaign organizer came to my house in the evening and, crying, appealed her pitiful situation. At her husband's workplace, they had declared that he should either control his wife well or leave his job, a choice between two options.

She cried, talking about her angry husband's actions, asking what would happen to her. I consoled that woman.

My candidacy made the realization of conscience and justice difficult and was creating the result of persecuting those who possessed conscience and justice.

From Seoul too, 5 comrades I had met during my Daejung Party days came to Busan to help me. Also, conscientious people I had never met before came from Seoul, from Daegu, from Daejeon.

They all exaggerated in the same way that public opinion and popularity for me were good, but my mind could not escape from depression.

A new fear that I had not felt before began to arise. There were many difficulties in making a decision at the crossroads of whether to go bankrupt for the sake of self-consolation or to defend myself for the sake of serving the future country, even if it meant disappointing sincere people.

As things went on, only 3 days were left until the final election day. Those 3 days were a greater pain to me than death. A certain degree of composure began to be restored in my mind.

I had to appease the backlash, no matter what, from the core members who had been running around diligently as organizational cells. So I called them all together in one place at the same time.

I laid bare my current feelings honestly.

"I do not want to deceive you. My position is a bit different from the other candidates.

Most of the other candidates are people that the other side likes. I am the opposite right now.

My own bankruptcy is something I am prepared for, but the clear fact that this will leave behind will not give me any excuse in the future.

My true heart wants to stand where you expect me to be. I know that the network and stems of the organization that you, who have little experience in campaigning, have created thinking of me in a short period of time, are considerable.

Even if I don't get elected, I also know the fact that the world's attention follows me.

But the problem that will follow the action I must choose now that I have reached the final stage is not a simple one.

It is whether you will carry the painful cross without regret. This is a state that is not decided for us."

The core members gathered in one place, unlike a moment ago, no one opened their mouths. Silence flowed on each other's faces.

The others also knew the election law and knew that the candidate they were working for was the conscientious person that the regime at that time feared the most. I began to convey my intentions again.

"I want to understand you in any case.

I am resolved not to resent you at all, even if you join hands with another candidate after this moment."

I had revealed my true heart.

The people who had gathered with some expectation left the office helplessly with disappointed faces.

The time, holding pain, begins to flow very, very slowly.

Every piece of news that came in was about the departure of the lower organization. For our group, the word 'best' was no longer left.
